قال الشارح : "و الخطاب فى اللغة "توجيه الكلام نحو الغير للإفهام "، ثم نقل إلى ما يقع به التخاطب ، وهو ههنا الكلام النفسى الأزلى ومن ذهب إلى أن الكلام لا يسمى في الأزل خطابا فسر الخطاب بالكلام الموجه للإفهام ، أو الكلام المقصود منه إفهام من هو متهيأ لفهمه .
تشریح: حکم کی تعریف میں جو ” خطاب" کا لفظ آیا ہے، شارح اس کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ "خطاب اپنے کلام کو سمجھانے کے لیے غیر کی طرف متوجہ کرنے کو کہتے ہیں پھر ہر اس کلام کو کو بھی "خطاب" کہا جانے لگا جس سے دوسرے کو خطاب کیا جاتا ہے۔ یہاں کلام سے مراد چونکہ ازلی و قدیم ہے اور ازل میں تو کوئی مخاطب نہیں تھا کہ اس کو خطاب کیا جائے گا اس لیے دو تو جیہوں میں سے ایک تو جیہ کرنی پڑے گی (1) لكلام الموجه للإفهام یعنی ایسا کلام جس کو سمجھانے کے لیے متوجہ کیا گیا ہو باقی مخاطب کا بر وقت موجود ہونا ضروری نہیں (۲) الکلام المقصود منه إفهام من هو متهيأ لفهمه یعنی ایسا کلام جس سے دوسرے کو سمجھانے کا قصد کیا گیا ہو یہاں پر بھی مخاطب کا بر وقت موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے۔
قال الشارح : "ومـعـنـى تعلقه بأفعال المكلفين " تعلقه بفعل من أفعالهم ، وإلالم يوجد حكم أصلا ، إذلا خطاب يتعلق بجميع الأفعال ، فدخل خواص النبي صلى الله . عليه وسلم كإباحة ما فوق الأربع من النساء ، وخرج خطاب الله المتعلق بأحوال ذاته وصفاته وتنزيهاته ، وغير ذلك مما ليس بفعل المكلف ..
تشریح: یہاں سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ آپ نے حکم کا معنی خـطـاب اللـه المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بیان کیا ہے افعال جمع ہے اور المكلفين " بھی جمع معرف باللام ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ حکم کہا جائے گا جو جمیع مکلفین کے جمیع افعال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو، یہ تو بہت مشکل ہے، کیونکہ ایک وقت میں ایک ہی خطاب جمیع مکلفین کے جمیع افعال کے ساتھ کس طرح متعلق ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب دیا کہ " افعال “ اور ”مکلفین" دونوں لفظ جمع ہے ہیں مگر اب ان میں جمع والا معنی نہیں رہا جنس فعل اور جنس مکلف مراد ہے لہذا اب حکم کی تعریف نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خواص مثلا چار سے زائد بیویوں کے ساتھ نکاح کا جائز ہونا اس کو شامل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس پر حکم تعریف خطاب الله المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بھی صادق آ رہی ہے۔ آخر میں بسأفعال المکلفین کی قید کا فائدہ بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں اس قید کے لگانے سے وہ خطابات خارج ہو گئے جو اللہ تعالیٰ کی ذات وصفات کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں۔
قال الشارح : "لا يقال إضافة الخطاب إلى الله تعالى يدل على أن لا حكم إلا ...
The address of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of obligated persons is the definition of the shar'i ruling as conventionally used among usuliyyun, not the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. The author held that it is its definition and that 'shar'i' is an additional qualifier on 'address of Allah', and that it being a definition of the shar'i ruling is merely the opinion of some Ash'aris. All this is due to their not perusing their books. So we say: Some Ash'aris defined the shar'i ruling as the address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons.
Commentary: First a reality is stated, then an objection is raised against the matn. The reality is that in all Shafi'i books, 'address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons... etc.' is made the definition of the shar'i ruling (hukm shar'i), not merely the definition of hukm (ruling) as taken in the definition of fiqh. But the author fell into two misconceptions: one that according to the Shafi'is, 'address of Allah... etc.' is only the definition of hukm, not of hukm shar'i, so the qualifier 'shar'i' would be superfluous because 'address of Allah' itself conveys the meaning of shar'i; second, that the definition according to some Shafi'is is only of hukm and according to others of hukm shar'i — i.e., they are not agreed on one. The commentator says: The author did not study their books; if he had paged through them, these misconceptions would never have occurred. The reality is that according to all Shafi'is, 'address of Allah' is the definition of the conventional shar'i ruling, not merely of hukm.
The commentator said: "And khatab (address) in language is 'directing speech towards another for understanding,' then it was transferred to that by which address occurs, and here it is the eternal speech of the soul. And whoever holds that speech is not called address in pre-eternity interprets khatab as speech directed for understanding, or speech from which understanding is intended for one who is prepared to understand it."
Commentary: Regarding the word 'khatab' in the definition of hukm, the commentator explains: 'Khatab means to direct one's speech towards another for understanding. Then every speech by which one addresses another came to be called khatab. Since the speech referred to here is pre-eternal and ancient, and in pre-eternity there was no addressee to be addressed, one of two interpretations must be adopted: (1) speech directed for understanding — the addressee need not exist at the time; (2) speech from which understanding is intended for one who is prepared to understand it — here too the addressee need not exist at the time.'
The commentator said: "And the meaning of 'its relation to the actions of obligated persons' is its relation to one of their actions; otherwise, no ruling exists at all, since no address relates to all actions. Thus, the special qualities of the Prophet, peace be upon him, such as the permissibility of marrying more than four women, enter, and the address of Allah related to the states of His essence, attributes, and transcendence, and other than that which is not the action of an obligated person, exits."
Commentary: Here is an answer to a question. The question is: You have expressed the meaning of hukm as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons'; 'af'al' is plural and 'al-mukallafin' is also plural with the definite article, implying that hukm is said to relate to all actions of all obligated persons. This is very difficult because how can a single address relate to all actions of all obligated persons at one time? The answer given is that both words 'af'al' and 'mukallafin' are plural, but here the plural meaning is not intended; rather, the genus of action and the genus of obligated person are meant. Therefore, the definition now includes the special qualities of the Prophet, such as the permissibility of marrying more than four women, because the definition 'address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons' also applies to it. Finally, the benefit of the qualifier 'related to the actions of obligated persons' is to exclude those addresses that relate to the essence and attributes of Allah.
The commentator said: "It is not said that the addition of 'the address' to 'Allah' indicates that there is no ruling except...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a definition and clarification of the term 'hukm sharʿī' (sharʿī ruling) as used in uṣūl al-fiqh. The author of the matn (based text) mistakenly claimed that the definition 'khiṭāb Allāh al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' (the address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons) is only for 'ḥukm' (ruling) and not for 'ḥukm sharʿī', and that the addition of 'sharʿī' is redundant. He also claimed that among the Ashʿarīs there is disagreement: some define only 'ḥukm' and others define 'ḥukm sharʿī'. The commentator (shāriḥ) refutes this by stating that all Ashʿarīs consistently use this definition for 'ḥukm sharʿī', and the author's error stems from not studying their books carefully. The commentator then explains the term 'khiṭāb' (address). In language, it means directing speech towards another for understanding. Since the speech of Allah is eternal and pre-eternal, and in pre-eternity no addressee existed, two interpretations are necessary: either it is speech directed for understanding (even if the addressee does not exist at that time), or it is speech intended for understanding by one who is prepared to understand (again, without requiring contemporaneous existence). Next, the phrase 'mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' is discussed. The plural forms 'afʿāl' (actions) and 'mukallafīn' (obligated persons) are not meant collectively (all actions of all people) but generically (any action of any obligated person). Thus, the definition includes special rulings for the Prophet (e.g., marrying more than four women) because those are actions of a mukallaf (the Prophet is obligated to follow commandments, though he has some special permissions). The qualifier also excludes addresses that relate to Allah's essence, attributes, or transcendence, as these are not actions of mukallafīn. The passage ends with a statement about not objecting that the addition of 'khiṭāb' to 'Allāh' implies that no ruling exists except... (the text cuts off). The overall point is to correct a misunderstanding and precisely define the scope of 'ḥukm sharʿī'.

Key Terms
خطاب الله (khiṭāb Allāh): The eternal, pre-eternal speech of Allah (kalam nafsi) that is directed towards creation for their understanding, considered as an address even if the addressee does not exist at the time of utterance.
حكم شرعي (ḥukm sharʿī): The address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons, as conventionally defined by usuliyyun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the correct definition of 'hukm shar'i' according to all Ash'aris?
A) The address of Allah related to all actions of all obligated persons collectively.
B) The address of Allah related to actions of obligated persons, understood generically.
C) The ruling established by analogy (qiyas).
D) The definition of fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm shar'i is 'khiṭāb Allāh al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn', and the Ash'ari school agrees on this definition.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Understanding 'Khiṭāb' and 'Afʿāl al-Mukallafīn' in the Definition of Hukm
Explains the meaning of 'khiṭāb' and the generic interpretation of 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'khiṭāb' in the definition refers to Allah's eternal speech and why 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn' is interpreted generically, and identify the legal implications.

Core Idea
The definition's terms are carefully chosen: 'khiṭāb' encompasses Allah's pre-eternal address and 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn' is generic, not collective.

This lesson dives deeper into the two key terms of the definition. Understanding the linguistic and usul nuances of 'khiṭāb' and the generic sense of 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn' is crucial for applying the definition correctly and avoiding scope errors.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the term 'khiṭāb'
Linguistically, 'khiṭāb' means directing speech toward another for understanding. Technically, it refers to what is used for address (al-mukhāṭabah). In this context, it is Allah's eternal speech (kalam nafsi).
2
Resolve the pre-eternity issue
Since Allah's speech is eternal, there was no addressee in pre-eternity. The commentator gives two interpretations: (a) speech directed for understanding, even if the addressee does not exist; (b) speech intended for one who is prepared to understand.
3
Analyze 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn'
The plural with definite article could indicate all actions of all mukallafīn, but that would be impossible. The commentator clarifies that it is for the genus (jins): any action of any mukallaf.
4
Identify what enters and exits
The definition includes special rulings for the Prophet (e.g., marrying more than four) because it is an action of a mukallaf. It excludes addresses about Allah's essence and attributes.
5
Reflect on the usul principle
The plural 'afʿāl' with 'al-' can indicate genus. This is a key hermeneutic rule in Hanafi usul.

خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين تعريف للحكم الشرعي المتعارف بين الأصوليين ، لا للحكم المأخوذ في تعريف الفقه ، والمصنف ذهب إلى أنه تعريف له ، وأن الشرعي قيد زائد على خطاب الله وإن كونه تعريفا للحكم الشرعي إنما هو رأى بعض الأشاعرة . وكل ذالك لعدم تصفحهم كتبهم فنقول : عرف بعض الأشاعرة الحكم الشرعى بخطاب الله المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين .
تشریح: اولاً ایک حقیقت بیان کی ہے اور اس کے بعد ماتن پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ حقیقت یہ ہے کہ تمام کتب شوافع میں ”خطاب الله المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين ... إلخ کو احکم الشرعی کی تعریف بنایا گیا ہے نہ کہ صرف حکم کی تعریف، جو فقہ کی تعریف میں ماخوذ ہے، لیکن ماتن کو یہاں پر دو مغالطے لگے ایک یہ کہ شوافع کے نزدیک "خطاب الله ... إلخ » صرف حکم کی تعریف ہے نہ کہ الحکم الشرعی کی لہذا اس وقت شرعی کی قید زائد ہوگی کیونکہ ”خطاب الله خود شرعی کے معنی کو ادا کر رہا ہے، دوسرا یہ کہ تعریف بعض شوافع کے نزدیک صرف حکم کی ہے اور بعض دوسرے حضرات کے نزدیک الحکم الشرعی کی یعنی وہ کسی ایک پر متفق نہیں ۔ شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ ماتن نے ان کی کتب کا مطالعہ نہیں کیا اور اگر ان کی کتابوں کی ورق گردانی کرتے تو ان کو یہ مغالطے ہر گز نہ لگتے واقعہ یہ ہے کہ تمام شوافع کے نزدیک خطاب اللہ حکم شرعی متعارف کی تعریف ہے نہ کہ صرف حکم کی۔
قال الشارح : "و الخطاب فى اللغة "توجيه الكلام نحو الغير للإفهام "، ثم نقل إلى ما يقع به التخاطب ، وهو ههنا الكلام النفسى الأزلى ومن ذهب إلى أن الكلام لا يسمى في الأزل خطابا فسر الخطاب بالكلام الموجه للإفهام ، أو الكلام المقصود منه إفهام من هو متهيأ لفهمه .
تشریح: حکم کی تعریف میں جو ” خطاب" کا لفظ آیا ہے، شارح اس کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ "خطاب اپنے کلام کو سمجھانے کے لیے غیر کی طرف متوجہ کرنے کو کہتے ہیں پھر ہر اس کلام کو کو بھی "خطاب" کہا جانے لگا جس سے دوسرے کو خطاب کیا جاتا ہے۔ یہاں کلام سے مراد چونکہ ازلی و قدیم ہے اور ازل میں تو کوئی مخاطب نہیں تھا کہ اس کو خطاب کیا جائے گا اس لیے دو تو جیہوں میں سے ایک تو جیہ کرنی پڑے گی (1) لكلام الموجه للإفهام یعنی ایسا کلام جس کو سمجھانے کے لیے متوجہ کیا گیا ہو باقی مخاطب کا بر وقت موجود ہونا ضروری نہیں (۲) الکلام المقصود منه إفهام من هو متهيأ لفهمه یعنی ایسا کلام جس سے دوسرے کو سمجھانے کا قصد کیا گیا ہو یہاں پر بھی مخاطب کا بر وقت موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے۔
قال الشارح : "ومـعـنـى تعلقه بأفعال المكلفين " تعلقه بفعل من أفعالهم ، وإلالم يوجد حكم أصلا ، إذلا خطاب يتعلق بجميع الأفعال ، فدخل خواص النبي صلى الله . عليه وسلم كإباحة ما فوق الأربع من النساء ، وخرج خطاب الله المتعلق بأحوال ذاته وصفاته وتنزيهاته ، وغير ذلك مما ليس بفعل المكلف ..
تشریح: یہاں سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ آپ نے حکم کا معنی خـطـاب اللـه المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بیان کیا ہے افعال جمع ہے اور المكلفين " بھی جمع معرف باللام ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ حکم کہا جائے گا جو جمیع مکلفین کے جمیع افعال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو، یہ تو بہت مشکل ہے، کیونکہ ایک وقت میں ایک ہی خطاب جمیع مکلفین کے جمیع افعال کے ساتھ کس طرح متعلق ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب دیا کہ " افعال “ اور ”مکلفین" دونوں لفظ جمع ہے ہیں مگر اب ان میں جمع والا معنی نہیں رہا جنس فعل اور جنس مکلف مراد ہے لہذا اب حکم کی تعریف نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خواص مثلا چار سے زائد بیویوں کے ساتھ نکاح کا جائز ہونا اس کو شامل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس پر حکم تعریف خطاب الله المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بھی صادق آ رہی ہے۔ آخر میں بسأفعال المکلفین کی قید کا فائدہ بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں اس قید کے لگانے سے وہ خطابات خارج ہو گئے جو اللہ تعالیٰ کی ذات وصفات کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں۔
قال الشارح : "لا يقال إضافة الخطاب إلى الله تعالى يدل على أن لا حكم إلا ...
The address of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of obligated persons is the definition of the shar'i ruling as conventionally used among usuliyyun, not the ruling taken in the definition of fiqh. The author held that it is its definition and that 'shar'i' is an additional qualifier on 'address of Allah', and that it being a definition of the shar'i ruling is merely the opinion of some Ash'aris. All this is due to their not perusing their books. So we say: Some Ash'aris defined the shar'i ruling as the address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons.
Commentary: First a reality is stated, then an objection is raised against the matn. The reality is that in all Shafi'i books, 'address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons... etc.' is made the definition of the shar'i ruling (hukm shar'i), not merely the definition of hukm (ruling) as taken in the definition of fiqh. But the author fell into two misconceptions: one that according to the Shafi'is, 'address of Allah... etc.' is only the definition of hukm, not of hukm shar'i, so the qualifier 'shar'i' would be superfluous because 'address of Allah' itself conveys the meaning of shar'i; second, that the definition according to some Shafi'is is only of hukm and according to others of hukm shar'i — i.e., they are not agreed on one. The commentator says: The author did not study their books; if he had paged through them, these misconceptions would never have occurred. The reality is that according to all Shafi'is, 'address of Allah' is the definition of the conventional shar'i ruling, not merely of hukm.
The commentator said: "And khatab (address) in language is 'directing speech towards another for understanding,' then it was transferred to that by which address occurs, and here it is the eternal speech of the soul. And whoever holds that speech is not called address in pre-eternity interprets khatab as speech directed for understanding, or speech from which understanding is intended for one who is prepared to understand it."
Commentary: Regarding the word 'khatab' in the definition of hukm, the commentator explains: 'Khatab means to direct one's speech towards another for understanding. Then every speech by which one addresses another came to be called khatab. Since the speech referred to here is pre-eternal and ancient, and in pre-eternity there was no addressee to be addressed, one of two interpretations must be adopted: (1) speech directed for understanding — the addressee need not exist at the time; (2) speech from which understanding is intended for one who is prepared to understand it — here too the addressee need not exist at the time.'
The commentator said: "And the meaning of 'its relation to the actions of obligated persons' is its relation to one of their actions; otherwise, no ruling exists at all, since no address relates to all actions. Thus, the special qualities of the Prophet, peace be upon him, such as the permissibility of marrying more than four women, enter, and the address of Allah related to the states of His essence, attributes, and transcendence, and other than that which is not the action of an obligated person, exits."
Commentary: Here is an answer to a question. The question is: You have expressed the meaning of hukm as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons'; 'af'al' is plural and 'al-mukallafin' is also plural with the definite article, implying that hukm is said to relate to all actions of all obligated persons. This is very difficult because how can a single address relate to all actions of all obligated persons at one time? The answer given is that both words 'af'al' and 'mukallafin' are plural, but here the plural meaning is not intended; rather, the genus of action and the genus of obligated person are meant. Therefore, the definition now includes the special qualities of the Prophet, such as the permissibility of marrying more than four women, because the definition 'address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons' also applies to it. Finally, the benefit of the qualifier 'related to the actions of obligated persons' is to exclude those addresses that relate to the essence and attributes of Allah.
The commentator said: "It is not said that the addition of 'the address' to 'Allah' indicates that there is no ruling except...
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a definition and clarification of the term 'hukm sharʿī' (sharʿī ruling) as used in uṣūl al-fiqh. The author of the matn (based text) mistakenly claimed that the definition 'khiṭāb Allāh al-mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' (the address of Allah related to the actions of obligated persons) is only for 'ḥukm' (ruling) and not for 'ḥukm sharʿī', and that the addition of 'sharʿī' is redundant. He also claimed that among the Ashʿarīs there is disagreement: some define only 'ḥukm' and others define 'ḥukm sharʿī'. The commentator (shāriḥ) refutes this by stating that all Ashʿarīs consistently use this definition for 'ḥukm sharʿī', and the author's error stems from not studying their books carefully. The commentator then explains the term 'khiṭāb' (address). In language, it means directing speech towards another for understanding. Since the speech of Allah is eternal and pre-eternal, and in pre-eternity no addressee existed, two interpretations are necessary: either it is speech directed for understanding (even if the addressee does not exist at that time), or it is speech intended for understanding by one who is prepared to understand (again, without requiring contemporaneous existence). Next, the phrase 'mutaʿalliq bi-afʿāl al-mukallafīn' is discussed. The plural forms 'afʿāl' (actions) and 'mukallafīn' (obligated persons) are not meant collectively (all actions of all people) but generically (any action of any obligated person). Thus, the definition includes special rulings for the Prophet (e.g., marrying more than four women) because those are actions of a mukallaf (the Prophet is obligated to follow commandments, though he has some special permissions). The qualifier also excludes addresses that relate to Allah's essence, attributes, or transcendence, as these are not actions of mukallafīn. The passage ends with a statement about not objecting that the addition of 'khiṭāb' to 'Allāh' implies that no ruling exists except... (the text cuts off). The overall point is to correct a misunderstanding and precisely define the scope of 'ḥukm sharʿī'.

Key Terms
خطاب (khiṭāb): Speech directed towards another for understanding; technically, the speech of Allah as an address.
جنس (jins): Genus; the plural form indicating the kind or category, not all individuals collectively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the correct interpretation of 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn' in the definition of hukm shar'i?
A) It refers to all actions of all obligated persons collectively.
B) It refers to the genus of action and the genus of obligated person, meaning any action of any mukallaf.
C) It refers only to the actions of the Prophet.
D) It refers to actions that are explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm shar'i uses 'khiṭāb' to refer to Allah's eternal address and 'afʿāl al-mukallafīn' generically, ensuring broad applicability.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Refining the Definition of Hukm: Excluding Narratives
Defending and refining the definition of hukm against the objection of over-inclusivity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to APPLY the qualifiers of iqtida/takhyir or the aspect (haythiyya) to distinguish hukm from Quranic narratives.

Core Idea
A Quranic story is not a hukm because it lacks demand or choice.

The initial definition of hukm as 'Allah's address related to actions' is too broad; it includes stories and reports without legal demands. Two refinements were proposed to exclude them: adding 'by demand or choice' or using the 'aspect' of the address.

Guided Path
1
State the initial definition of hukm
Hukm is defined as khitab Allah related to the actions of the mukallaf. Note that this includes narratives (qisas) like the story of Pharaoh.
2
Identify the problem: the definition is not exclusive (ghayr mani')
The definition applies to Quranic stories and reports about actions, which are not considered hukm in terminology.
Example verse: 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96).
3
Explain the first refinement: add 'bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir'
This qualifier ensures the address contains a demand (obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike) or a choice (permission). Narratives lack these, so they are excluded.
Iqtida includes wajib, mandub, haram, makruh; takhyir covers mubah.
4
Explain the second refinement: use the 'aspect' (haythiyya)
The definition is understood as 'address related to actions from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallaf'. Narratives relate to actions from other aspects (e.g., admonition, refutation), so they are excluded without an extra qualifier.
This relies on the phrase 'min haythu huwa fi'lu al-mukallaf'.
5
Compare the two refinements
The first adds an explicit condition; the second relies on an implicit aspect. Both achieve the same goal of excluding narratives.
The passage notes that some say the second suffices, eliminating the need for the qualifier.

تشریح اس عبارت میں ایک سوال اور اس کا جواب دینا مقصود ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ حکم کا معنی خطاب اللہ ہے اور خطاب کی اضافت لفظ اللہ کی طرف ہے اور قانون ہے کہ اضافت اختصاص کا فائد دیتی ہے اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ خطاب صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کا ہوتا ہے اور وہی واجب الاطاعت ہے حالانکہ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا حکم بھی واجب الاطاعتہ ہے اور اولی الامر یعنی حاکم اور علماء کا حکم بھی واجب الاطاعۃ ہوتا ہے اسی طرح آقا کا حکم غلام کے لیے واجب الا طاعۃ ہوتا ہے۔ جواب: نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم یا اولی الامر اور سردار، ان تمام کی اطاعتہ در حقیقت اللہ تعالی کے حکم دینے کی وجہ سے واجب اور ضروری ہوئی ہے لہذا ان کا حکم خطاب اللہ ہی ہے۔

قال الشارح : ثم اعترض على هذا التعريف بأنه غير مانع ، لأنه تدخل فيه القصص المبينة لأحوال المكلفين وأفعالهم ، والأخبار المتعلقة بأعمالهم ، كقوله تعالى (والله خلقكم وما تعملون) مع أنها ليست أحكاما ، فزيد على التعريف قيد يخصصه ، ويخرج ما دخل فيه من غير أفراد المحدود ، وهو قولهم : "بالاقتضاء أو التخيير" فإن تعلق الخطاب بالأفعال في القصص والاخبار عن الأعمال ليس تعلق الاقتضاء أو التخيير ، إذ معنى "التخيير" إباحة الفعل والترك للمكلف ، ومعنى الاقتضاء طلب الفعل مع المنع عن الترك وهو الإيجاب ، أو بدونه وهو الندب ، أو طلب الترك مع المنع عن الفعل وهو التحريم ، أو بدونه وهو الكراهة ، وقد يجاب بأنه لا حاجة إلى زيادة قولهم: بالاقتضاء أو التخيير ، لأن قيد الحيثية مراد . والمعنى خطاب الله المتعلق بفعل المكلف من حيث هو فعل المكلف ، وليس تعلق الخطاب بالأفعال في صورة النقض من حيث أنها أفعال المكلفين وهو ظاهر.

تشریح اس عبارت سے غرض ایک سوال ذکر کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ آپ نے جو حکم کی تعریف کی ہے وہ مانع نہیں کیونکہ یہ تعریف ان قصص و واقعات پر بھی صادق آ رہی ہے جن میں مکلفین کے افعال کا تذکرہ کیا گیا ہے، مثلا: فرعون نے فلاں کام کیا ،فلاں کام کو چھوڑا ، اسی طرح یہ تعریف ان اخبار کو بھی شامل ہے جو متعلق بافعال المكلفين ہیں جس طرح والله خلقكم وما تعملون با وجود یکہ ان دونوں قسموں کو حکم اصطلاحی نہیں کہا جاتا اس اعتراض کے دو جواب دیے ہیں۔ اول: حکم کی تعریف صرف خطاب الله المتعلق بأفعال المکلفین نہیں بلکہ اس میں ایک قید زائد کا اضافہ کرتے ہیں وہ بالاقتضاء او التخيير ہے اب حکم کی تعریف کا مفہوم یہ ہوگا کہ حکم اس خطاب اللہ کو کہتے ہیں جس میں مکلف سے کسی کام کے کرنے کا تقاضا کیا گیا ہو یا اختیار دیا گیا ہو ظاہر بات ہے کہ قصص میں جو خطاب ہوتا اس میں کسی بھی کی طلب وغیرہ نہیں ہوتی بلکہ کوئی واقعہ مخاطب کے ذہن میں ڈالا جاتا ہے بس کوئی مطالبہ نہیں ہوتا ۔ [روم؟] بالاقتضا أو التخییر کی قید بڑھانے کی ضرورت نہیں بلکہ یہاں پر حیثیت کی قید ملحوظ و مراد ہے کہ قصص کے اندر جو خطاب ہوتا ہے وہ اس حیثیت سے نہیں ہوتا کہ افعال المكلفين ہیں بلکہ اس حیثیت سے ہوتا ہے کہ ان میں وعظ و نصیحت اور عبرت کا سامان ہے، اس لیے اللہ تعالی فرماتے ہیں (فاعتبروا يا أولى الالباب) اسی طرح وہ اخبار جو متعلق بأفعال المكلفين ہوں جیسے (والله خلقكم وما تعملون) یہاں پر خطاب بھی الحیثیت سے نہیں بلکہ اس حیثیت سے ہے کہ جمیع افعال کے خالق اللہ تعالی ہے در حقیقت ان لوگوں پر ادا کرتا ہے جو کہتے تھے کہ بندہ اپنے افعال کا خود خالق ہے۔

قال الشارح : قوله : "زاد البعض اعترضت المعتزلة على هذا التعريف بثلثة أوجه : الأول: أن الخطاب عندكم قديم ، والحكم حادث، لكونه متصفا بالحصول بعد العدم كقولنا : حلت المرأة بعد ما لم تكن حلالا ، ولكونه معللا بالحادث كقولنا حلت بالنكاح و حرمت بالطلاق . الثاني : أنه يشمل على كلمته "أو" وهي للتشكيك والترديد والتحديد . الثالث : أنه غير جامع للأحكام الوضعية ، مثل سببية دلوك الشمس لوجوب الصلاة ، وشرطية الطهارة لها ، ومانعية النجاسة عنها. والمصنف أهمل ذكر المانعية في تفسير.
Commentary: The purpose of this passage is to present a question and its answer. The question is: The meaning of hukm is khitab Allah, and the addition of khitab is to the word Allah, and the rule is that addition gives specification. This means that khitab is only from Allah, and He alone is obligatory to obey, whereas the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is also obligatory to obey, and the command of ulul-amr (ruler and scholars) is also obligatory to obey, similarly the master's command is obligatory for the slave. Answer: The obedience to the Prophet, ulul-amr, and master is in reality obligatory because of Allah's command, so their command is also khitab Allah.

The commentator said: Then an objection was raised against this definition that it is not exclusive (mani'), because it includes stories (qisas) that describe the states and actions of the mukallafun, and reports (akhbar) related to their deeds, like His statement (And Allah created you and what you do) while they are not rulings. So a qualifier was added to the definition to specify it and exclude what entered from non-individuals of the defined, which is their saying: 'by demand or choice (bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir)'. For the attachment of the address to actions in stories and reports about deeds is not an attachment of demand or choice. Indeed, the meaning of 'choice' is permission of the action and omission for the mukallaf, and the meaning of 'demand' is requesting the action with prevention from omission, which is obligation (ijab), or without it which is recommendation (nadb), or requesting omission with prevention from action, which is prohibition (tahrim), or without it which is dislike (karaha). And it may be answered that there is no need to add their saying 'by demand or choice', because the qualifier of aspect (haythiyya) is intended. And the meaning is: the address of Allah related to the action of the mukallaf from the aspect that it is the action of the mukallaf. And the attachment of the address to actions in the case of the counterexample is not from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallaf, and that is clear.

Commentary: The purpose of this passage is to mention a question and answer it. The question is: The definition of hukm you gave is not exclusive (mani'), because this definition applies also to stories and events in which the actions of the mukallafun are mentioned, e.g., Pharaoh did such and such, left such and such. Similarly, this definition includes reports related to the actions of the mukallafun, like 'And Allah created you and what you do', even though these two types are not called hukm in terminology. Two answers are given to this objection. First: The definition of hukm is not only 'the address of Allah related to the actions of the mukallafun', but an extra qualifier is added to it, which is 'by demand or choice'. Now the meaning of the definition of hukm is: hukm is that address of Allah in which the mukallaf is demanded to do something or given a choice. It is obvious that in stories, the address does not contain any demand, but rather an event is placed in the mind of the addressee, no demand. [Rom?] There is no need to add the qualifier of iqtida or takhyir, but rather here the qualifier of aspect (haythiyya) is intended and meant: The address in stories is not from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallafun, but from the aspect that they contain admonition, advice, and lesson. Therefore, Allah says: 'So take lesson, O people of insight'. Similarly, reports related to the actions of the mukallafun, like 'And Allah created you and what you do', here the address is not from that aspect, but from the aspect that Allah is the Creator of all actions, in reality it is a refutation of those who said that the servant is the creator of his own actions.

The commentator said: His saying: 'Some added: The Mu'tazila objected to this definition on three grounds: First: The address (khitab) with you is eternal (qadim), while the ruling (hukm) is temporal (hadith), because it is described as coming into existence after non-existence, as we say: 'She became permissible after she was not permissible', and because it is caused by a temporal event as we say: 'She became permissible by marriage and prohibited by divorce'. Second: It includes the word 'or' which indicates doubt, hesitation, and limitation. Third: It does not include the status-based rulings (ahkam wad'iyyah), such as the sun's declining as a cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer, the condition (shart) of purification for it, and the preventer (mani') of impurity from it. And the author omitted the mention of preventer (man'iyyah) in the interpretation.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of hukm (ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first addresses a preliminary question: If hukm is defined as Allah's address, then how can the commands of the Prophet, rulers, scholars, and masters be considered binding? The answer is that their authority is derived from Allah's command, so all binding address ultimately traces back to Allah.

Then the sharh (commentary) turns to a technical objection: The definition of hukm as 'Allah's address related to the actions of the mukallaf' is not exclusive (ghayr mani'), because it would include narratives (qisas) and reports (akhbar) about the actions of past nations or general statements about human actions, such as the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do'. These are not considered hukm in the technical sense because they do not impose a demand or grant a choice.

To remedy this, some scholars add the qualifier 'bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir' (by demand or choice). This ensures that only addresses that either require an action (obligation, recommendation) or forbid an action (prohibition, dislike) or give permission are considered hukm. Narratives merely report events without such demand, so they are excluded.

Another response without adding that qualifier is to consider the 'aspect' (haythiyya) of the address. The definition is understood as 'address related to the actions of the mukallaf from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallaf'. In qisas, the actions are mentioned from the aspect of lesson and admonition, not from the aspect of being actions of the mukallaf to which a ruling applies. Similarly, in the verse about creation, the address is about refuting those who deny Allah's creative power, not about prescribing a ruling.

Finally, the Mu'tazila raise three objections: (1) The address (khitab) is eternal, but the ruling (hukm) is temporal, as it comes into existence after non-existence (e.g., a woman becomes halal after being haram). (2) The word 'or' (aw) in the qualifier suggests doubt or hesitation. (3) The definition does not cover status-based rulings (ahkam wad'iyyah) like cause (sabab), condition (shart), and preventer (mani'). The passage ends by noting that the author (al-Taftazani or Sadr al-Shariah?) omitted mentioning the preventer in his interpretation, implying a need for further discussion.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The address of Allah related to the actions of the mukallaf, either by demand (iqtida) or choice (takhyir), or from the aspect of being actions of the mukallaf.
اقتضاء (iqtida): Demand; the quality of an address that requires the mukallaf to do or refrain from an action.
تخيير (takhyir): Choice; the quality of an address that gives the mukallaf the option to do or not do an action (ibaha).
حيثية (haythiyya): Aspect or perspective; the consideration from which the address is related to actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following verses is correctly categorized as hukm after adding the qualifier 'by demand or choice'?
A) 'Indeed, the righteous will be in pleasure' (82:13)
B) 'O you who have believed, fulfill [all] contracts' (5:1)
C) 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96)
D) 'The example of those who were entrusted with the Torah' (62:5)

Key Takeaway
Hukm is Allah's address that demands or allows an action; narratives are excluded either by adding the qualifier 'by demand or choice' or by considering the aspect of the address.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
The Mu'tazila Objections to the Definition of Hukm
Presentation and analysis of the three Mu'tazila objections to the definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EVALUATE the three Mu'tazila objections to the definition of hukm and explain the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila argue that hukm is temporal and excludes status-based rulings; Hanafis maintain the definition captures the primary type.

After the definition of hukm was refined, the Mu'tazila raised three objections: (1) the address (khitab) is eternal but the ruling (hukm) is temporal; (2) the word 'aw' in the qualifier suggests doubt; (3) the definition does not include cause, condition, and preventer (ahkam wad'iyyah). This lesson examines each objection and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the first Mu'tazila objection: temporal nature of hukm
The Mu'tazila argue that khitab is eternal (qadim) whereas hukm is temporal (hadith) because it comes into existence after non-existence, e.g., 'she becomes permissible after not being permissible'. This challenges the definition equating hukm with khitab.
2
State the second objection: the word 'aw' indicates doubt
The qualifier 'bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir' uses 'aw' (or), which the Mu'tazila claim introduces hesitation or indecision, inappropriate for a precise definition.
3
State the third objection: exclusion of ahkam wad'iyyah
The definition does not include status-based rulings such as cause (sabab), condition (shart), and preventer (mani') — e.g., the sun's declining as a cause for prayer.
Note: The original author omitted man'iyyah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to each objection
For (1): The ruling is derived from the eternal address and is temporal; this does not invalidate the definition. For (2): 'aw' can be used for division (taqsim) not doubt. For (3): Some Hanafi scholars later include wad'iyyat as a separate category or incorporate them into the definition.
The commentator notes that the omission of man'iyyah is a lacuna.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute affects whether sabab, shart, mani' are considered hukm in the same sense as taklifi rulings. Hanafis treat them as hukm wad'i, distinct from hukm taklifi.
This distinction is important in deriving rulings and understanding the structure of legal obligation.

And it may be answered that there is no need to add their saying 'by demand or choice', because the qualifier of aspect (haythiyya) is intended. And the meaning is: the address of Allah related to the action of the mukallaf from the aspect that it is the action of the mukallaf. And the attachment of the address to actions in the case of the counterexample is not from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallaf, and that is clear.

Commentary: The purpose of this passage is to mention a question and answer it. The question is: The definition of hukm you gave is not exclusive (mani'), because this definition applies also to stories and events in which the actions of the mukallafun are mentioned, e.g., Pharaoh did such and such, left such and such. Similarly, this definition includes reports related to the actions of the mukallafun, like 'And Allah created you and what you do', even though these two types are not called hukm in terminology. Two answers are given to this objection. First: The definition of hukm is not only 'the address of Allah related to the actions of the mukallafun', but an extra qualifier is added to it, which is 'by demand or choice'. Now the meaning of the definition of hukm is: hukm is that address of Allah in which the mukallaf is demanded to do something or given a choice. It is obvious that in stories, the address does not contain any demand, but rather an event is placed in the mind of the addressee, no demand. [Rom?] There is no need to add the qualifier of iqtida or takhyir, but rather here the qualifier of aspect (haythiyya) is intended and meant: The address in stories is not from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallafun, but from the aspect that they contain admonition, advice, and lesson. Therefore, Allah says: 'So take lesson, O people of insight'. Similarly, reports related to the actions of the mukallafun, like 'And Allah created you and what you do', here the address is not from that aspect, but from the aspect that Allah is the Creator of all actions, in reality it is a refutation of those who said that the servant is the creator of his own actions.

The commentator said: His saying: 'Some added: The Mu'tazila objected to this definition on three grounds: First: The address (khitab) with you is eternal (qadim), while the ruling (hukm) is temporal (hadith), because it is described as coming into existence after non-existence, as we say: 'She became permissible after she was not permissible', and because it is caused by a temporal event as we say: 'She became permissible by marriage and prohibited by divorce'. Second: It includes the word 'or' which indicates doubt, hesitation, and limitation. Third: It does not include the status-based rulings (ahkam wad'iyyah), such as the sun's declining as a cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer, the condition (shart) of purification for it, and the preventer (mani') of impurity from it. And the author omitted the mention of preventer (man'iyyah) in the interpretation.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of hukm (ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first addresses a preliminary question: If hukm is defined as Allah's address, then how can the commands of the Prophet, rulers, scholars, and masters be considered binding? The answer is that their authority is derived from Allah's command, so all binding address ultimately traces back to Allah.

Then the sharh (commentary) turns to a technical objection: The definition of hukm as 'Allah's address related to the actions of the mukallaf' is not exclusive (ghayr mani'), because it would include narratives (qisas) and reports (akhbar) about the actions of past nations or general statements about human actions, such as the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do'. These are not considered hukm in the technical sense because they do not impose a demand or grant a choice.

To remedy this, some scholars add the qualifier 'bi'l-iqtida aw al-takhyir' (by demand or choice). This ensures that only addresses that either require an action (obligation, recommendation) or forbid an action (prohibition, dislike) or give permission are considered hukm. Narratives merely report events without such demand, so they are excluded.

Another response without adding that qualifier is to consider the 'aspect' (haythiyya) of the address. The definition is understood as 'address related to the actions of the mukallaf from the aspect that they are actions of the mukallaf'. In qisas, the actions are mentioned from the aspect of lesson and admonition, not from the aspect of being actions of the mukallaf to which a ruling applies. Similarly, in the verse about creation, the address is about refuting those who deny Allah's creative power, not about prescribing a ruling.

Finally, the Mu'tazila raise three objections: (1) The address (khitab) is eternal, but the ruling (hukm) is temporal, as it comes into existence after non-existence (e.g., a woman becomes halal after being haram). (2) The word 'or' (aw) in the qualifier suggests doubt or hesitation. (3) The definition does not cover status-based rulings (ahkam wad'iyyah) like cause (sabab), condition (shart), and preventer (mani'). The passage ends by noting that the author (al-Taftazani or Sadr al-Shariah?) omitted mentioning the preventer in his interpretation, implying a need for further discussion.

Key Terms
أحكام وضعية (ahkam wad'iyyah): Status-based rulings that are not direct demands or choices, but are causes (sabab), conditions (shart), or preventers (mani').
الخطاب (khitab): The divine address; speech directed by Allah to the mukallaf.
سببيّة (sababiyya): The property of being a cause (sabab) for a ruling.
شرطیة (shartiyya): The property of being a condition (shart) for a ruling.
مانعية (man'iyya): The property of being a preventer (mani') for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the Mu'tazila objections?
A) The address is eternal but the ruling is temporal
B) The definition includes narratives and stories
C) The word 'or' indicates doubt
D) The definition does not include sabab, shart, and mani'

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila objections highlight the need to differentiate between primary rulings (hukm taklifi) and status-based rulings (hukm wad'i), a distinction that later Hanafi scholars formalized.

The First Mu'tazili Objection and the Ash'ari Response on the Eternality of Hukm
Presenting the first Mu'tazili objection and the Ash'ari response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first Mu'tazili objection against defining hukm as khiṭāb Allāh and explain the Ash'ari response distinguishing between the eternal ruling and its temporal relation.

Core Idea
Hukm itself is eternal; only its relation to acts is new – causes are signs, not effectors.

The definition of hukm as Allah's eternal address seems to conflict with the obvious contingency of rulings: a woman becomes permissible after marriage, a prayer becomes obligatory after the call. The Mu'tazila seized on this to argue that hukm must itself be contingent. In this lesson, we examine their first objection and the classical Ash'ari/Hanafi response that preserves the eternality of the ruling by distinguishing the ruling itself from its manifest relation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under attack
State the Ash'ari/Hanafi definition of hukm as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of responsible persons by requirement or option.' This is the definition the Mu'tazila criticise.
The definition is from the matn; the passage later adds the restriction 'by requirement or option' to exclude stories.
2
Follow the Mu'tazili objection
Understand their argument: hukm is contingent because (a) it comes into existence after non-existence (e.g., 'she became permissible after she was not'), and (b) its causes are contingent (marriage, divorce). Therefore, hukm cannot be eternal.
The objection targets the apparent contradiction between the definition (eternal) and the observable contingency of rulings.
3
Analyse the Ash'ari response
Two denials: (a) It is the relation (ta'alluq) that becomes new, not the hukm itself. (b) Contingent causes do not effect the hukm; they are merely signs (amārāt) that indicate an already existing eternal ruling.
This distinguishes between the ruling's essence (eternal) and its manifestation in time.
4
Note the incomplete transmission
The response is cut off mid-sentence; the scholar would likely continue to explain how a contingent sign can indicate an eternal ruling without affecting it.
The second and third objections (about the word 'or' and wadi'i rulings) are not addressed in this excerpt.

The purpose of this passage is to mention a question and answer it. The question is that the definition you gave of hukm is not preventing [the inclusion of stories] because this definition applies to stories and events in which the actions of responsible persons are mentioned, e.g., Pharaoh did such and such, left such and such; similarly, this definition includes reports related to actions of responsible persons like 'And Allah created you and what you do.' These two types are not called hukm technically. Two answers are given to this objection. First: The definition of hukm is not only 'the address of Allah related to the actions of the responsible persons', but they add an extra restriction: 'by requirement or option'. Now the meaning of the definition of hukm becomes: hukm is the address of Allah in which a responsible person is required to do something or given an option. It is clear that in stories the address does not contain any demand etc., rather a story is placed in the mind of the addressee, there is no demand. The restriction 'by requirement or option' does not need to be added; rather the restriction of aspect is intended: that the address in stories is not from the aspect that they are actions of responsible persons, but from the aspect that they contain admonition and lesson. Therefore Allah says: 'So take lesson, O people of insight'. Similarly, reports related to actions of responsible persons like 'And Allah created you and what you do' – here the address is not from that aspect but from the aspect that Allah is the creator of all actions, in reality it is a rebuttal against those who said that the servant is the creator of his own actions. The commentator said: His statement: 'Some added' – The Mu'tazila objected to this definition with three aspects: First: The address with you is eternal, but the ruling is contingent, because it is described as coming into existence after non-existence, as we say: 'She became permissible after she was not permissible', and because it is caused by what is contingent, as we say: 'She became permissible by marriage and prohibited by divorce'. Second: It includes the word 'or' which indicates doubt, hesitation, and limitation. Third: It does not include the wadi'i rulings, such as the causativeness of the sun's declination for the obligation of prayer, the conditionality of purity for it, and the preventiveness of impurity from it. The author omitted mentioning preventiveness in the explanation of wadi'i address. Explanation: From here, he transmits three objections from the Mu'tazila against the definition of hukm. The first objection: Hukm is contingent, because previously it is non-existent then comes into existence, as it is said: 'She became permissible after she was not permissible' – here 'permissibility' is a hukm that came to the woman after marriage. The second reason for its being contingent: The causes of the hukm are contingent; whatever is caused by something contingent is itself contingent. For example, the cause of permissibility is marriage and the cause of prohibition is divorce. Since marriage and divorce are contingent, their effects (permissibility and prohibition) are also contingent. So the gist of the objection is: When hukm is contingent, defining it as 'address of Allah' is wrong, because the address of Allah is eternal. The second objection: In defining hukm, the word 'or' is used ('by requirement or option'), whereas in definitions the use of the word 'or' is incorrect because 'or' gives doubt, so the purpose of definition is not achieved. The third objection: The definition of hukm is not comprehensive, because one type of hukm is wadi'i hukm, which means that something is a cause for something else, e.g., 'the sun's declination for prayer' – 'declination' means the sun's descent from zenith; or something is a preventer for something else, like impurity is a preventer for prayer – the author omitted this example in the text; or something is a condition for something, like purity is a condition for prayer. In any case, these are forms of wadi'i hukm, but your definition of hukm does not include them. The commentator said: The Ash'ari responded to the first [objection] by denying that the hukm is described as coming to be after non-existence; rather what is described thus is the relation [ta'alluq]. The meaning is the relation of permissibility to her after it was not related, and by denying that the hukm is caused by the contingent in the sense of the contingent having an effect on it; rather its meaning is that the contingent is a sign and identifier for it; for legal causes are signs and identifiers, not necessitators and effectors. And the contingent is suitable...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from Dars-e-Talweeh is a commentary on the definition of hukm (ruling) in usul al-fiqh. It presents three objections raised by the Mu'tazila against the Ash'ari/Hanafi definition of hukm as 'the address of Allah related to the actions of responsible persons by requirement or option'. The first objection argues that hukm is contingent (hādith) because it comes into existence after non-existence (e.g., a woman becomes permissible after marriage) and because its causes are contingent (marriage, divorce). Since the address of Allah (khiṭāb Allāh) is eternal (qadīm), defining hukm as the address leads to a contradiction. The second objection notes that the definition uses the word 'or' (aw), which introduces doubt and is inappropriate for a rigorous definition. The third objection states the definition fails to include al-ahkām al-waḍʿiyya (declaratory rulings) such as causality (sababiyya), condition (sharṭiyya), or preventiveness (māniʿiyya). The Ash'ari response to the first objection begins by denying that hukm itself is described as coming after non-existence; rather it is the 'relation' (taʿalluq) of the hukm to its subject that becomes new. They also deny that contingent causes truly effect the hukm; rather they are merely signs (amārāt) and identifiers (muʿarrifāt) of it, not efficient causes. This aligns with the Ash'ari (and Hanafi) position that divine rulings are eternal in God's knowledge, and temporal events only trigger their manifestation. The passage is cut off mid-sentence at 'و الحادث يصلح' (and the contingent is suitable...), likely continuing to explain how a contingent sign can indicate an eternal ruling.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this context, hukm is the object of dispute: Ash'ari/Hanafi define it as an eternal divine attribute; Mu'tazila define it as contingent.
خطاب الله (khiṭāb Allāh): The address of Allah, which is eternal (qadīm) according to Ash'ari/Hanafi theology.
معتزلة (Muʽtazila): A theological school that argued rulings are contingent, denying eternal attributes.
علة (ʿilla): A cause; in usul, the 'illa is the effective cause for a ruling. Here the Mu'tazila see it as an efficient cause; Ash'ari see it as a sign (amāra).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The definition includes the word 'or'.
B) The definition does not include waḍʿī rulings.
C) The hukm is contingent while the divine address is eternal.
D) The definition applies to stories and reports.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili objection that hukm is contingent is answered by the Ash'ari distinction: the ruling itself is eternal, only its relation to the act is new, and causes are mere signs.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Defending the Definition of Hukm: Including Wad'i Rulings
Defending the definition of hukm against three Mu'tazilite objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Mu'tazilite objections to the definition of hukm and evaluate the Hanafi positions regarding the inclusion of wad'i rulings.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of hukm must explicitly include wad'i rulings because taklifi and wad'i are distinct categories.

The definition of hukm (divine ruling) is foundational to usul al-fiqh. This passage presents three Mu'tazilite objections to the standard definition and two Hanafi responses: one that subsumes wad'i under taklifi and another that adds 'aw al-wad'' explicitly. The author prefers the latter, underscoring the precision required in legal terminology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections
The Mu'tazilites raise objections concerning the eternity of hukm vs. temporal acts, the use of 'aw' (or) suggesting doubt, and the exclusion of wad'i rulings from the definition.
2
Analyze the first response
The response argues that nikah/talaq are signs (amarat) not causes; they reveal the eternal ruling without causing it.
This uses the distinction between cause and sign.
3
Examine the second response
The response clarifies that 'aw' here indicates division (taqsim) not doubt, as hukm is of two types: demand and choice.
4
Contrast the two responses to the third objection
Response (a) claims wad'i is implicitly included in iqtida' or takhyir; response (b) says wad'i is a distinct category requiring explicit mention.
5
Grasp the author's tarjih
The author (musannif) chooses response (b): the correct definition must add 'aw al-wad'' because the two categories are conceptually different.

إمارة ، ومعرفة للقديم كالعالم للصانع . وعن الثاني : بأن "أو" هنا تقسيم المحدود . وتفصيله؛ لأنه نوعان نوع له تعلق الاقتضاء ونوع له تعلق التخيير فلا يمكن جمعهما في حد واحد بدون التفصيل . وأما الثالث : فالتزمه بعضهم، وزاد في التعريف قيدا يعمه ، ويجعله شاملا للحكم الوضعى فقال بالاقتضاء أو التخيير أو الوضع أى وضع الشارع وجعله .
تشريح
معتزلہ کے ان تینوں اعتراضات کا جواب بالترتیب یوں دیا گیا ہے کہ جس طرح خطاب اللہ قدیم ہے، اسی طرح حکم بھی قدیم ہے البتہ اس کا تعلق حادث ہے مطلب یہ ہوا کہ حلت و حرمت قدیم ہیں البتہ بندہ سے ان کا تعلق اب ہوا جب کہ نکاح یا طلاق کا واقعہ پیش آیا باقی یہ کہ حلت و حرمت کی علتیں حادث ہیں تو ان کو بھی حادث ہونا چاہیے اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ نکاح یا طلاق ململ نہیں بلکہ امارات و معرفات ہیں علت وہ ہوتی ہے جو معلول میں مؤثر ہو اور معلول کو پیدا کر رہی ہوا مارت یا معرف وہ کہلاتی ہے جس سے معلول کا صرف علم آ جائے باقی اس کو پیدا کرنے والی نہ ہو قدیم کے لیے معرف یا امارۃ حادث ہو سکتی ہے جیسا کہ عائم ذات باری کے لیے معرف ہے کیونکہ اس سے ذات باری کا ہمیں وجود معلوم ہوتا ہے باقی اس کے وجود کو پیدا کرنے والا نہیں کیونکہ اللہ تعالی اپنے وجود میں کسی کا محتاج نہیں ہے تو اب نکاح اور طلاق نے ہمیں حلت اور حرمت کا علم تو حاصل ہوا ہے باقی حلت و حرمت کو نکاح یا طلاق نے پیدا نہیں کیا۔ دوسرے سوال کا جواب دیا ہے کہ "أو" جس طرح تشکیک (شک ڈالنے) کے لیے آتا ہے اسی طرح کبھی تقسیم و تنویع کیلیے آتا ہے تو یہاں پر کیونکہ حکم کی تقسیم کر ناتھی اس لیے "أو" کو استعمال کیا اور معنی تقسیم والا مراد ہے نہ کہ تشکیک اور تردید کا۔ تیسرے سوال کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ بعض حضرات نے معتزلہ کے اس سوال کو تسلیم کرتے ہوئے "أو الوضع" کی قید بڑھانے کو کہا ہے تا کہ حکم کی تعریف عام وشامل ہو تو اسوقت حکم کی تعریف یوں ہوگی "خطاب الله المتعلق بأفعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء أو التخيير أو الوضع".
قال الشارح : "وأجاب بعضهم : بأنا لا نسلم أن خطاب الوضع حكم ، ونحن لا نسميه حكما ، وإن اصطلح غيرنا على تسميته حكما ، فلا مشاحة معه ، وعليه تغيير التعريف. ولو سلم فلا نسلم خروجه عن الحد ، فإن مرادنا من الاقتضاء أو التخيير أعم من الصريحي والضمني وخطاب الوضع قبيل الضمني ؛ إذ معنى سببية الدلوك وجوب الصلاة عنده معنى شرطية الطهارة ، وجوبها في الصلاة أو حرمة الصلوة بدونها . معنى مانعية النجاسة حرمة الصلوة معها أو وجوب إزالتها حالة الصلوة كذا في جميع الأسباب والشر والموانع .
تشريح
بعض حضرات نے اس آخری سوال کا جواب اور طرح دیا ہے وہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہم حکم وضعی کو سرے سے حکم ہی تسلیم نہیں کرتے تو اگر اس کو حکم کی تعریف شامل نہ ہو تو کیا حرج ہے کیونکہ وہ حکم ہی نہیں اگر چہ اور لوگ اس کو حکم کہتے رہیں "لا مشاحة في الاصطلاحات" ہم اس کو حکم ماننے کے لیے تیار نہیں اس لیے ہمارے نزدیک حکم کی تعریف بالکل درست ہے، اگر وہ حکم کی تعریف میں تبدیلی کرتے ہیں تو بلاشک کریں۔ اور اگر بالفرض ہم تسلیم کر لیں یہ حکم ہے، تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ "بالاقتضاء" کی قید میں داخل ہے لہذا اس کے لیے کوئی اور قید لگانے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ باقی اس میں کس طرح داخل ہے وہ یوں کہ اقتضاء سے مراد عام ہے چاہے صراحتا اس حکم میں کسی کام کے کرنے کا تقاضا کیا گیا ہو یا ضمنا تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ سبیت یا شرطیت یا مانعیت جو احکام وضعی تھے ان میں فنی طور پر مطالبہ ہے کہ جب سورج کا دلوک ہو تو نماز پڑھو۔ اس طرح جب نماز پڑھو تو طہارت کو ضرور حاصل کرو۔ اس طرح نجاست کے ہوتے ہوئے نماز نہ پڑھو یا نجاست کا دور کرنا بوقت ارادہ صلاۃ ضروری ہے بہر حال اسباب و شروط اور مانعات کے اندر اس قسم کی تاویل کر کے ان کو اقتضاء میں داخل کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
قال الشارح : "وذهب المصنف إلى أن الحق زيادة القيد لأن الخطاب نوعان تكليفى ووضعى ، فلما ذكر أحدهما وجب ذكر الآخر ، ولا وجه لجعل الوضعي داخلا في الاقتضا أو التخيير أى فى التكليفي ، لأنهما مفهومان متغايران ، ولزوم أحدهما للآخر في بعض الصور لا يدل على اتحادهما . وأنت خبير بأنه لا توجيه لهذا الكلام أصلا . أما
[Arabic:] It is a sign and an identifier for the eternal, like the world is a sign for the Creator. Regarding the second [objection]: that 'or' here is a division of the limited [definition]. Its detail: because it is of two types: a type that has a relation of demand and a type that has a relation of choice, so they cannot be combined in one limit without detail. As for the third: some accepted it and added in the definition a condition that includes it and makes it comprehensive to include the wad'i ruling, saying: by demand or choice or position, i.e., the position of the Lawgiver and His making. [Urdu commentary explains the three objections: (1) Hukm is eternal like divine speech, only its relation to people is temporal; nikah and talaq are signs (amarat) not causes; (2) 'or' is for division, not doubt; (3) some scholars add 'or wad'' to include wad'i rulings. Then the sharh says: 'And some answered: we do not accept that wad'i address is a ruling, and we do not call it a ruling; even if others term it a ruling, there is no quarrel; and then the definition would be changed. Even if we accept it as a ruling, we do not accept its exclusion from the definition; our intended meaning of demand or choice is general, both explicit and implicit, and wad'i address is of the implicit type; for example, the causality of the sun's declination implies the obligation of prayer, the conditionality of purity implies its obligation in prayer or the prohibition of prayer without it, the preventiveness of impurity implies the prohibition of prayer with it or the obligation to remove it during prayer, and so on for all causes, conditions, and preventers.' Then the Urdu commentary explains this and then the sharh says: 'And the author held that the truth is to add the condition because address is of two types: taklifi and wad'i; when one is mentioned, the other must be mentioned; and there is no way to make wad'i included in demand or choice, i.e., in taklifi, because they are two distinct concepts; the entailment of one by the other in some cases does not indicate their unity. And you know that there is no justification for this speech at all. As for...']
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a scholastic debate on the definition of hukm (divine ruling). The commentator (sharih) sets out three Mu'tazilite objections to the standard definition and answers them. First, if hukm is defined as divine speech (kalam) which is eternal, how can it relate to temporal acts? The response is that hukm is eternal in essence but its connection (ta'liq) to actions is temporal; temporal events like marriage or divorce are merely indicators (amarat/ma'rifat) that reveal the eternal ruling without causing it. Second, the use of 'aw' (or) in the definition suggests doubt or choice, but it is here used for division (taqsim) between demand and choice. Third, the definition fails to include wad'i rulings (like causality, conditionality, preventiveness). Two responses are given: (a) Some scholars accept this and add 'aw al-wad'' (or positional ruling) to the definition; (b) others argue that wad'i rulings are not truly rulings but merely implicit within the taklifi categories. The sharh then presents the author's (musannif's) position: the correct view is to add the condition because taklifi and wad'i are fundamentally distinct categories; one cannot be subsumed under the other even if they sometimes overlap. This passage is essential for understanding the Hanafi classification of hukm and the methodological precision required in defining legal terms.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): Divine address (khitab Allah) relating to the actions of mukallaf by way of demand, choice, or position.
الحكم الوضعي (al-hukm al-wad'i): A ruling that does not involve demand or choice but establishes a thing as a cause (sabab), condition (shart), or preventer (mani') for another ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (musannif) in this passage, what should be added to the definition of hukm to include wad'i rulings?
A) The word 'aw' between iqtida' and takhyir.
B) The phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or positional ruling).
C) The phrase 'wa al-wad'' (and positional ruling).
D) Nothing; wad'i is already included in iqtida'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm must explicitly include wad'i rulings because they are a separate category from taklifi rulings.

Including al-Hukm al-Wad'i in the Definition of Hukm
Debate on including hukm wad'i in definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the two positions on including al-hukm al-wad'i in the definition of hukm and apply the conceptual distinction between taklifi and wad'i.

Core Idea
Hukm wad'i is a distinct concept from hukm taklifi — it cannot be reduced to implicit demand without distorting its meaning.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih presents a usul dispute: should the definition of hukm include al-hukm al-wad'i (declaratory rulings like cause, condition, preventer) or is it already covered under iqtida' (demand)? Some scholars deny wad'i is a ruling at all; others try to subsume it under taklifi. The commentator, likely Taftazani, critiques both views, siding with the author (Sadr al-Shariah) that the restriction 'al-wad'' is necessary. Understanding this debate sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi usul categorizes divine addresses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
First, read the passage to identify the claim that hukm wad'i is not a ruling at all, and the alternative claim that it falls under iqtida' (implicit demand). Note how each side argues.
The first view denies wad'i as hukm; the second accepts it but tries to absorb it into taklifi.
2
Examine the commentator's critique
The commentator responds with two arguments: (1) if wad'i is denied as a ruling, there's no obligation to include it; (2) if it is a ruling, taklifi and wad'i are conceptually distinct, so including wad'i under iqtida' is forced.
He calls the opposing view 'without justification' – strong language in usul discourse.
3
Understand the conceptual distinction
Taklifi rulings directly demand action (e.g., pray, avoid). Wad'i rulings establish relationships (e.g., if X happens, Y becomes obligatory) without direct demand. Mixing them conflates two different functions.
Example: 'sun's declination' is a cause (sabab) for prayer – it does not directly demand prayer but triggers the obligation.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether categories like sabab, shart, mani' are considered legal rulings. In Hanafi usul, they are; excluding them from the definition would narrow the scope of hukm.
This affects how jurists derive rulings – e.g., causality in contracts or purity.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
The authoritative Hanafi position (taught here) is that hukm includes both taklifi and wad'i. The definition must mention 'wad'' to be complete.
This lesson reinforces the Hanafi usul structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض حضرات نے اس آخری سوال کا جواب اور طرح دیا ہے وہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہم حکم وضعی کو سرے سے حکم ہی تسلیم نہیں کرتے تو اگر اس کو حکم کی تعریف شامل نہ ہو تو کیا حرج ہے کیونکہ وہ حکم ہی نہیں اگر چہ اور لوگ اس کو حکم کہتے رہیں " لا مشاحة في الاصطلاحات " ہم اس کو حکم ماننے کے لیے تیار نہیں اس لیے ہمارے نزدیک حکم کی تعریف بالکل درست ہے، اگر وہ حکم کی تعریف میں تبدیلی کرتے ہیں تو بلاشک کریں۔ اور اگر بالفرض ہم تسلیم کر لیں یہ حکم ہے، تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ "بالاقتضاء کی قید میں داخل ہے لہذا اس کے لیے کوئی اور قید لگانے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ باقی اس میں کس طرح داخل ہے وہ یوں کہ اقتضاء سے مراد عام ہے چاہے صراحتا اس حکم میں کسی کام کے کرنے کا تقاضا کیا گیا ہو یا ضمنا تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ سبیت یا شرطیت یا مانعیت جو احکام وضعی تھے ان میں فنی طور پر مطالبہ ہے کہ جب سورج کا دلوک ہو تو نماز پڑھو۔ اس طرح جب نماز پڑھو تو طہارت کو ضرور حاصل کرو۔ اس طرح نجاست کے ہوتے ہوئے نماز نہ پڑھو یا نجاست کا دور کرنا بوقت ارادہ صلاۃ ضروری ہے بہر حال اسباب و شروط اور مانعات کے اندر اس قسم کی تاویل کر کے ان کو اقتضاء میں داخل کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
قال الشارح : " وذهب المصنف إلى أن الحق زيادة القيد لأن الخطاب نوعان تكليفى ووضعى ، فلما ذكر أحدهما وجب ذكر الآخر ، ولا وجه لجعل الوضعي داخلا في الاقتضا أو التخيير أى فى التكليفي ، لأنهما مفهومان متغايران ، ولزوم أحدهما للآخر في بعض الصور لا يدل على اتحادهما . وأنت خبير بأنه لا توجيه لهذا الكلام أصلا . أما أولا فلأن المنع يمنع كون الخطاب الوضعى حكما ويصطلح على تسمية بعض أقسام الخطاب حكما دون البعض فكيف يجب عليه ذكر الوضعى في تعريف الحكم بل كيف يصح . وأما ثانيا : فلأنه يمنعه كونه خارجا عن التعريف ويجعل الخطاب التكليفي أعم منه شاملا له فأى ضرر له في تغاير مفهومهما بل كيف يتحد مفهوم العام والخاص على أن قوله المفهوم من الخطاب الوضعى تعلق شئ بشئ فيه تسامح . والمعنى أن المفهوم منه الخطاب بتعلق شئ بشئ بكونه سببا أو شرطا أو مانعا
Some scholars have given a different answer to this last question. They say: We do not at all accept al-hukm al-wad'i as a ruling. So if it is not included in the definition of hukm, what harm is there? Because it is not a ruling, even if other people keep calling it a ruling: 'there is no dispute in terminology.' We are not prepared to accept it as a ruling, so according to us the definition of hukm is completely correct. If they want to change the definition of hukm, let them do so without doubt. And if we assume we accept that it is a ruling, then we say: it is included in the restriction of 'by way of demand' (bi'l-iqtida'), so there is no need to add any other restriction for it. As for how it is included, it is that iqtida' is general, whether the demand is explicit (sarih) in that ruling to perform an action or implicit (dimni). So we say that causality (sababiyya), conditionality (shartiyya), or preventiveness (mani'iyya), which were the declaratory rulings (ahkam wad'iyya), contain technically a demand: when the sun's declination (duluk) occurs, pray. Similarly, when you pray, necessarily obtain purity. Similarly, in the presence of impurity do not pray, or remove impurity at the time of intending prayer is necessary. In any case, by interpreting (ta'wil) in this way within causes (asbab), conditions (shurut), and preventers (mawani'), they can be included within iqtida'.
The commentator said: "The author (al-musannif) held that the correct view is to add the restriction (qayd) [of wad'] because address (khitab) is of two types: taklifi and wad'i. So when one of them is mentioned, the other must be mentioned. There is no justification for making the wad'i included within iqtida' or takhyir, i.e., within taklifi, because the two concepts are distinct. The necessity of one for the other in some cases does not indicate their unity. And you are fully aware that this statement has no justification at all. Firstly, because the denier denies that the wad'i address is a ruling and conventionally names some divisions of address as 'ruling' and not others; so how can it be obligatory upon him to mention wad'i in the definition of hukm? Indeed, how can it be valid? Secondly, because he prevents it from being outside the definition and makes the taklifi address more general, inclusive of it. So what harm is there to him in the distinction of their concepts? Rather, how can the concept of general and specific be unified? Moreover, his statement 'the understood from the wad'i address is the attachment of a thing to a thing' contains laxity. And the meaning is: the understood from it is the address regarding the attachment of a thing to a thing by being a cause, condition, or preventer."
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the definition of hukm (legal ruling) and whether al-hukm al-wad'i (declaratory/status ruling) should be included. The discussion is part of the commentary on Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah, with the commentator (probably Taftazani) critiquing the author's position. Some earlier scholars argued that al-hukm al-wad'i is not a ruling at all, so no need to include it in the definition. Others accepted it but tried to show it falls under 'bi'l-iqtida'' (by way of demand) through interpretation of causes, conditions, and preventers as implicitly demanding actions. The author (al-musannif) held that the definition must include the word 'al-wad'' to cover declaratory rulings. The commentator rejects both positions, arguing that first, if one denies wad'i is a ruling, there is no need to mention it; second, if one accepts it as a ruling but claims it's included under iqtida', then the conceptual distinction between taklifi and wad'i remains, so adding 'al-wad'' is still necessary. The dispute reflects different views on whether the definition of hukm should be broad enough to include both types or limited to taklifi.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): A legal ruling; the address of the Lawgiver concerning the actions of the subjects by way of demand (iqtida'), choice (takhyir), or declaratory status (wad').
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A declaratory ruling that establishes something as a cause (sabab), condition (shart), or preventer (mani') without a direct demand for action.
اقتضاء (iqtida'): Demand; one of the modes of taklifi address, which can be explicit (sarih) or implicit (dimni).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the main flaw in the argument that hukm wad'i can be included under iqtida'?
A) Wad'i rulings are not demanded at all.
B) The concepts of taklifi and wad'i are distinct, and inclusion under iqtida' does not unite them.
C) The author never mentioned iqtida'.
D) All scholars agree wad'i is not a ruling.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm in Hanafi usul must encompass both taklifi and wad'i rulings; attempts to reduce wad'i to implicit demand fail due to conceptual distinctness.

Refutation of Adding 'Wad'' to the Definition of Hukm
Refuting the author's proposal to include wad'i hukm via the word 'wad''

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Ash'ari positions on the inclusion of wad'i hukm in the definition of hukm, and identify the key terminological dispute regarding 'iqtida'.

Core Idea
Adding 'wad'' is unnecessary: either wad'i is not hukm, or 'iqtida' already encompasses it.

In this passage, the commentator refutes the author's proposal to add the word 'wad'' to the definition of hukm to include declaratory rulings. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) had argued that since taklifi and wad'i are conceptually distinct, both must be mentioned. The commentator raises two objections: first, the Asha'ira do not recognize wad'i as hukm at all; second, even if they did, the term 'iqtida' in the definition is broad enough to cover it. This lesson unpacks the debate over the scope of hukm and the precise meaning of 'iqtida'.

Guided Path
1
State the author's proposal
Identify the author's claim: to include wad'i hukm, the definition of hukm must add the qualification 'wad'' alongside 'iqtida'.
The author is Sadr al-Shariah, representing a Hanafi perspective.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position on wad'i hukm
Recognize that the Asha'ira do not consider declaratory speech as hukm; for them, hukm is exclusively prescriptive.
This is the first objection: if wad'i is not hukm, adding 'wad'' is irrelevant.
3
Analyze the second objection regarding 'iqtida'
Understand the commentator's argument that 'iqtida' is general enough to include both explicit and implicit demands, thus covering wad'i if it were accepted.
The broad interpretation of 'iqtida' eliminates the need for separate mention.
4
Evaluate the example of 'human' and 'rational'
Examine how the commentator uses the example to show that two concepts can differ yet coincide in application, so the author's insistence on conceptual difference does not necessitate separate definitional mention.
This rebuts the author's claim that wad'i must be explicitly named.
