Definition of Shar'i Ruling: Avoiding Tautology
Textual analysis of the definition of shar'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school defines al-shar'i as 'what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver' and identify the tautology problem avoided by this definition.

Core Idea
Defining shar'i as 'what is conveyed by the address' would be a tautology because hukm itself is the address of Allah.

This passage examines the technical definition of 'shar'i' (legal) in usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains why the author chose a definition that explicitly excludes rationally known matters. This choice prevents logical repetition with the definition of hukm and highlights a key difference with the Ash'ari school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two candidate definitions for al-shar'i
The text contrasts two possible definitions: (1) 'what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver' and (2) 'what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver'. Recognize the first as potentially tautological.
2
Understand why the first definition leads to tautology
Since hukm itself is defined as 'the address of Allah' (khiṭāb Allāh), defining shar'i as 'what is conveyed by the address' would be repeating the same concept. The Hanafi definition avoids this by using a different phrase.
3
Apply the Hanafi definition to examples
The definition includes rulings from direct text and analogy, and excludes obligations known by reason alone (e.g., obligation of faith). Test this: consensus and analogy are shar'i because they depend on divine address indirectly.
4
Contrast with the Ash'ari position
Ash'aris deny reason's role in knowing good and evil, so for them all rulings are equally dependent on revelation. Thus, their definition 'what is conveyed by the address' effectively means the same as the Hanafi definition, but if they also define hukm as khiṭāb Allāh, the term 'shar'i' becomes redundant.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis can call analogical rulings 'shar'i' explicitly, while Ash'aris might face a tautology in their terminology. The Hanafi definition is more precise for usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : "قوله : والشرعية ما يدرك لو لا خطاب الشارع بنفس الحكم أو بأصله المقيس عليه فيخرج عنها مثل وجوب الإيمان ، ويدخل مثل كون الإجماع، والقياس حجة على تقدير أن يكون حكما . وإنما لم يفسر الشرعية بما ورد به خطاب الشرع لأن التقدير أن الحكم مفسر بخطاب الله ... إلخ وح يكون تقييده بالشرعى تكرارا .وعند الأشاعرة ما ورد به خطاب الشرع في قوة ما لا يدرك لو لا خطاب الشارع ، إذ لا مجال للعقل في درك الأحكام عندهم ، فلو كان خطاب الله الخ تعريفاً للحكم على ما زعم المصنف لا للحكم الشرعي لكان ذكر الشرعي تكرارا البته بأي تفسير فسر. تشریح: متن کی توضیح و تشریح کر رہے ہیں مصنف نے "الشرعیہ“ میں تقسیم کی کہ خواہ خطاب شارع اس حکم میں ہو یا اس کے اصل اور مقیس علیہ کے اندر ہو تو حکم قیاسی بھی ”الشرعبہ " کی قید میں داخل ہو جائے گا باقی وجوب ایمان خارج ہو جائے گا کیونکہ وہ اس معنی میں شرعی نہیں قیاس اور اجماع کا حجتہ ہوتا اگر ان کو حکم میں داخل مانا جائے تو یہ بھی داخل ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ شرعی ہیں اور عملیہ کی قید سے خارج ہو جائیں گے کمامر انما لم يفسر ... إلخ سے فرماتے ہیں کہ ماتن نے ”الشرعیہ کا معنی ” مالا يدرك لو لا خطاب الشارع “ سے کیا ہے ”ماورد به خطاب الشارع “ سے کیوں نہیں کیا؟ فرماتے ہیں اس لیے کہ حکم کا معنی "خطاب الله " گویا کہ "مارود به الخطاب" کے معنی میں ہے اور اگر شرعی کا بھی یہی کرتے ہیں تو شرعی کی قید مکر ز بنتی ہے باقی اشاعرہ حضرات کے نزدیک چونکہ تمام احکام شرعی ہیں اور عقل کو ان کے حسن و قبح معلوم کرنے کی کچھ طاقت نہیں۔ یہ بات ہم عنقریب بیان کریں گے اس لیے ان کے نزدیک ”الشرعی کا معنی ما ورد به خطاب الشارع ہوگا سے اس کا مطلب بھی ”لو لا خطاب الشارع" ہی ہے لہذا اگر خطاب الله ... الخ مطلق حکم کی تعریف بنائیں جس طرح مصنف کو کا خیال ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ مطلق حکم کی یہی تعریف کرتے ہیں تو ”الشرعی“ کی قید تکرار ہے خواہ اس كا حسن "مالا يدرك لولا خطاب الشارع “ سے کریں یا ”ماورد به خطاب الشارع“ سے کریں، کیونکہ ہم اوپر بتلا آئے ہیں کہ اشاعرہ کے نزدیک عقل کو بالکل احکام میں دخل نہیں ۔ تمام احکام کا دارو مدار شریعت پر ہے۔ نتیجہ یہ نکلا کہ اشاعرہ کے نزدیک تمام احکام شرعیه مالا يدرك لولا خطاب الشارع “ کے قبیل سے ہیں۔
The commentator said: "His statement: 'And al-shar'iyya (the legal ruling) is that which is not known except by the address of the Lawgiver, either by the ruling itself or by its origin (the thing measured upon), so it excludes such as the obligation of faith, and includes such as the probative value of consensus and analogy, assuming they are rulings. And he did not define al-shar'iyya as what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver because the assumption is that the ruling is defined by the address of Allah... etc., so restricting it with 'shar'i' would be tautology. And according to the Ash'aris, what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver has the force of what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver, since there is no scope for reason in knowing rulings according to them. So if the address of Allah etc. is a definition of the ruling as the author claims, not the legal ruling, then mentioning 'shar'i' would be a tautology regardless of which interpretation is taken." Explanation: The text is being clarified and explained. The author divided "al-shar'iyya" stating that whether the address of the Lawgiver concerns this ruling or its origin and the thing measured upon, then the analogical ruling also enters the restriction of "al-shar'iyya". The remaining obligation of faith is excluded because it is not shar'i in this sense. Consensus and analogy are proofs; if they are considered to be included in the ruling, they would also enter because they are shar'i, and they would be excluded by the restriction of 'amaliyya (practical). The phrase "he did not define... etc." explains that the author defined al-shar'iyya as "what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver" and not as "what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver". He says: because the meaning of hukm is "the address of Allah", so it is as if it is in the meaning of "what is conveyed by the address", and if shar'i is also given the same meaning, then the restriction of shar'i becomes tautology. As for the Ash'aris, since all rulings are shar'i and reason has no power to know their good and evil—this will be explained soon—therefore, according to them, the meaning of al-shar'i is "what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver" which also means "what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver". Thus, if the address of Allah etc. is made the definition of the absolute ruling as the author thinks some Ash'aris define it, then the restriction of al-shar'i is tautology whether it is interpreted as "what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver" or "what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver", because we have already stated that according to the Ash'aris reason has absolutely no entry into rulings. All rulings depend on the Shari'ah. The result is that according to the Ash'aris all shar'i rulings belong to the category of "what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver".
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the definition of 'shar'i' (legal) ruling. The commentator (sharh) explains why the matn (text) defined al-shar'iyya as 'what is not known without the address of the Lawgiver' (mā lā yudrak law lā khiṭāb al-shāri') rather than 'what is conveyed by the address of the Lawgiver' (mā warada bihi khiṭāb al-shāri'). The reason is that the term 'hukm' (ruling) itself is already defined as 'the address of Allah' (khiṭāb Allāh), so defining al-shar'iyya as 'what is conveyed by the address' would be a tautology (takrār). The commentator then discusses the Ash'ari position: since they deny reason's role in discerning good and evil, all rulings are effectively 'what is not known without the address', even if they define it differently. The passage concludes that for Ash'aris, the restriction 'shar'i' would be redundant if the absolute ruling is defined as the address of Allah. This is a careful exercise in usul terminology to avoid logical repetition.

Key Terms
الشرعیہ (al-shar'iyya): The legal ruling that is not known without the address of the Lawgiver, either directly or via analogy.
حکم (hukm): The address of Allah (khiṭāb Allāh) concerning the actions of the accountable individuals.
خطاب الشارع (khiṭāb al-shāri'): The address of the Lawgiver (Allah or His Messenger) which is the source of legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the former includes analogical rulings
B) Because the latter would be tautological with the definition of hukm
C) Because the Ash'aris prefer the former definition
D) Because the latter excludes the obligation of faith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of al-shar'i excludes rationally known obligations and avoids tautology with the definition of hukm.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Defining Fiqh: Necessary Knowledge vs. Deductive Faculty
Debate on excluding necessary knowledge from fiqh definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether necessary religious knowledge is included in the definition of fiqh and explain why the Hanafis consider the condition excluding it redundant.

Core Idea
Fiqh is a faculty of deduction, not mere knowledge; necessary truths are automatically excluded.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: should the definition of fiqh explicitly exclude knowledge of necessary religious matters such as the obligation of prayer and fasting? The Hanafi matn argues that such a condition is superfluous because fiqh is a faculty (malaka) that requires ijtihad, not a collection of known rulings. The Shafi'i commentator defends the condition as a clarification of their school's position. Understanding this debate sharpens your grasp of what it means to be a faqih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested element
The dispute concerns whether the definition of fiqh must include a condition excluding 'necessary religious knowledge' (daruriyyat al-din). The matn objects to Imam al-Razi's condition in al-Mahsul that fiqh applies only to rulings not known necessarily.
The opposing school here is Shafi'i (Imam al-Razi and al-Taftazani).
2
Understand the Hanafi position
Hanafis define fiqh as a faculty (malaka) to derive rulings. Even knowing many deductive issues without this faculty does not make one a faqih. Therefore, excluding one necessary issue is redundant; the definition already implies that fiqh is not mere knowledge.
The matn emphasizes that fiqh is not 'knowledge of some rulings' but a faculty of deduction.
3
Understand the Shafi'i counter-argument
The Shafi'i commentator (Taftazani) argues that Imam al-Razi's condition is not restrictive but clarificatory: it states the Shafi'i convention that fiqh is about non-evident, deductive rulings. It does not imply that without it, necessary knowledge would be included.
Taftazani distinguishes between a condition that excludes (iḥtirāzī) and one that explains (taḥrīrī).
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects whether one who knows only necessary rulings (e.g., prayer obligation) can be called a faqih. Both schools say no, but for different reasons: Hanafi: lacks faculty; Shafi'i: lacks deduction. The dispute is mostly conceptual.
No practical difference in fatwa, but it reflects each school's emphasis on the nature of fiqh.
5
Note the incomplete second objection
The passage begins a new objection about the term 'ahkam' (rulings) but is cut off. This lesson focuses only on the first objection regarding necessary knowledge.
The second objection likely questions whether 'ahkam' means all, some, or a proportion of rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہیں بلکہ علم الاخلاق (تصوف) میں سے ہیں علامہ تفتازانی افول ... الخ سے رد کر رہے ہیں کہ فقہ کی تعریف ان پر صادق نہیں آتی "عملیہ " کی قید سے خارج ہورہے ہیں، کیونکہ مذکورہ احکام تو نفسانی و روحانی ملکات کہ یا تو مصنف کو وہاں پر لگائی گئی "عملا " کی قید بھول گئی یا یہاں پر الشرعية کے بعد العملیہ کی قید کو نظر انداز کر رہے ہیں۔ لا يعد من قال الشارح : " قوله لا يزاد عليه المصطلح بين الشافعية أن العلم بالأحكام إنما يسمى فقها إذا كان حصوله بطريق النظر والاستدلال ، حتى أن العلم بوجوب الصلوة والصوم ، ونحو ذالك مما اشتهر كونه من الدين بالضرورة بحيث يعلمه المتدين وغيره - الفقه اصطلاحا ، ولهذا يذكرون قيد الاكتساب أو الاستدلال والإمام قيد في المحصول الأحكام بالتي لا يعلم كونها من الدين بالضرورة وقال: هو احتراز عن العلم بوجوب الصلاة والصوم أنه لا يسمى فقها معنى أنه لا يدخل في مسمى الفقه ولا يعد عنه على ما صرح بها الإمام فى قيد العملية، لا بمعنى أنه لم يحترز عنه لزم أن يكون العالم بمجرد وجوبهما فقها على ما فهمه الصنف، فاعترض بمنع لزوم ذلك بناء على أن الفقيه من له الفقه . والفقه ليس علما ببعض الأحكام . وإن قيل حتى يكون العالم بمسئلة أو مسئلتين فقيها بل العالم بمائة مسئلة غريبة استدلالية وحدها لا يسمى فقها ثم إذا كان اصطلاحهم على أن الـعـلـم بضروريات الدين ليس من الفقه ، فلا بد من إخراجها عن تعريفهم للفقه ، فلا يكون القيد المخرج لها ضائعا ، ولا القول : بكونها من الفقه صحيحا عندهم ، ولا اصطلاح على ذالك صالحا للاعتراض عليهم . تشريح مائن نے امام رازی کے ایک قید بڑھانے پر اعتراض کیا تھا۔ شارح یہاں سے ماتن کا رد کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ شوافع کے نزدیک فقہ ایسے احکام کے جاننے کا نام ہے جو بطریقِ استدلال و اکتساب حاصل ہوں، اس لیے فقہ کی تعریف میں بالاستدلال کی قید بڑھائی تھی تا کہ بدیہی شرعی احکام مثلا نماز ، روزہ حج اور زکوۃ وغیرہ فقہ کی تعریف سے خارج ہو جائیں کیونکہ عالم ، جاہل ، دین دار ، غیر دین دار سب جانتے ہیں مگر ان کے جاننے والے کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جاتا اس لیے امام رازی نے اپنی کتاب المحصول میں فقہ کی تعریف میں التي لا يعلم كونها من ضروريات الدین کی قید بڑھائی تھی بشر طیکہ وہ احکام بدیہات دین میں سے نہ ہوں۔ اس پر ماتن نے اعتراض کر ڈالا کہ یہ قید بڑھانا فضول ہے اس لیے کہ فقہ کوئی چند ایک مسائل کے جاننے کا نام نہیں تا کہ ان کو نکالنے کے لیے قید بڑھائی جائے ، بلکہ فرض کرو اگر ایک آدمی مسائل جانتا ہو پھر بھی اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا جب تک کہ اس میں ملکہ موجود نہ ہو چہ جائیکہ نماز وروزہ جیسے بدیہی مسائل کے جاننے والے کو فقیہ کہیں، لہذا امام رازی کی قید بالکل لغو ہے۔ علامہ تفتازانی مانن پر رد کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ امام رازی نے اس قید کو احترازی نہیں بنایا کہ اگر اس قید کو نہ بڑھایا جاتا تو نماز اور روزہ جیسے بدیہی مسائل فقہ کی تعریف میں شامل ہو جاتے اور یہ کہ ان کا جانے والا فقیہ بن جاتا، بلکہ اس قید کے بڑھانے سے مقصد محض وضاحت کرنا اور اپنے مذہب کو بیان کرتا ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک فقہ چند مسائل بدیہی کے جاننے کا نام نہیں بلکہ نظری و استدلالی مسائل کو فقہ کہتے ہیں لہذا ایسی وضاحت کو کیونکر مدار اعتراض بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ قال الشارح : " قوله : ثم اعلم أنه لا يراد بالأحكام "اعتراض على تعريف الفقه بأن المراد بالأحكام إما الكل أى : المجوع ، وإما كل واحد ، وإما بعض له نسبة إلى الكل كالنصف أو الأكثر كالثلثين ، مثلا : اما البعض مطلقا وإن قل : والأقسام بإسرها باطلة أما الاول : فلان الحوادث، وإن كانت متناهية في نفسها بانقضاء دار التكليف إلا أنها لكثرتها ، وعدم انقطاعها مادامت الدينا غير داخلة تحت حصر الحاصرين ، وضبط المجتهدين ، وهو المعنى بقوله لا تكاد تتناهى فلا يعلم أحكامها جزئيا جزئيا لعدم ....
No, rather they are from the science of ethics (Sufism). Allama Taftazani is refuting ... that the definition of fiqh does not apply to them; they are excluded by the condition of 'amaliyya (practical), because these mentioned rulings are psychical and spiritual characteristics, not related to action. However, the author (matn) earlier, where he quoted from Abu Hanifa the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of the self, what is for it and against it', he said there that the condition of 'amaliyya should be added so that ethics is excluded, and he himself explicitly said: 'knowledge of the self, what is for it and against it from spiritual experiences' – these are spiritual actions, this is ethics and Sufism; and 'knowledge of the self, what is for it and against it from practical actions' – this is fiqh. So it is known that either the author forgot the condition of 'amaliyya he added there, or here he is ignoring the condition of 'amaliyya after shar'iyya. The commentator said: 'His statement: No addition is made to it. The term among the Shafi'is is that knowledge of rulings is called fiqh only if it is obtained through reflection (nazar) and deduction (istidlal), such that knowledge of the obligation of prayer and fasting and similar things that are well-known as necessary matters of religion, such that the religious and other know them – [that is not called] fiqh terminologically. For this reason they mention the condition of acquisition (iktisab) or deduction (istidlal). And Imam [al-Razi] in al-Mahsul conditioned the rulings that are not known to be from the necessary matters of religion, and he said: This is to avoid including knowledge of the obligation of prayer and fasting that it is not called fiqh, meaning it does not enter into the definition of fiqh and is not counted as it, according to what the Imam stated regarding the condition of practicality. Not that if he had not used this condition, it would necessarily follow that the one who knows just their obligation would be a faqih, as the author (matn) understood. So he objected by denying that necessity, based on the fact that a faqih is one who possesses fiqh, and fiqh is not knowledge of some rulings. Even if it is said that one who knows one or two issues is a faqih, rather one who knows a hundred rare deductive issues alone is not called a faqih. Then if their convention is that knowledge of necessary matters of religion is not from fiqh, it is necessary to exclude it from their definition of fiqh, so the condition that excludes is not wasted, nor is the statement that it is from fiqh correct according to them, nor is the convention of that suitable for objecting against them.' Explanation: The author objected to Imam al-Razi adding a condition. The commentator here intends to refute the author. The detail is that according to the Shafi'is, fiqh is the name for knowledge of rulings that are obtained through deduction and acquisition. Therefore, in the definition of fiqh, the condition of 'by deduction' was added so that evidentiary shar'i rulings such as prayer, fasting, Hajj, and Zakat, etc., would be excluded from the definition of fiqh because the learned, the ignorant, the religious, and the non-religious all know them, but the one who knows them is not called a faqih. For this reason, Imam al-Razi in his book al-Mahsul added the condition 'which are not known to be from the necessary matters of religion' in the definition of fiqh, provided that those rulings are not from the evident matters of religion. The author objected that this addition is superfluous because fiqh is not the name for knowing just a few issues such that a condition is needed to exclude them. Rather, suppose a person knows issues, still he will not be called a faqih unless he possesses the faculty (malaka) – let alone the one who knows evident issues like prayer and fasting. Therefore, Imam al-Razi's condition is absolutely useless. Allama Taftazani, in refuting the author, states that Imam al-Razi did not make this condition restrictive, i.e., that if this condition were not added, then prayer and fasting etc. would enter the definition and the one who knows them would become a faqih. Rather, the purpose of adding this condition is merely clarification and to express his own madhhab: that in his view, fiqh is not the name for knowing a few evident issues, but rather theoretical and deductive issues are called fiqh. So how can such clarification be made the subject of objection? The commentator said: 'His statement: Then know that what is meant by rulings (ahkam) is not...' This is an objection to the definition of fiqh that by 'rulings' is meant either all (i.e., the total), or each individual, or some parts that have a ratio to the whole like half or more like two-thirds, etc., or some parts absolutely even if few. All these divisions are invalid. As for the first: because events, although they are finite in themselves by the end of the abode of obligation, yet due to their abundance and continuity as long as the world lasts, they are not encompassed by any enumerator or control of mujtahids. This is the meaning of his statement: they are almost limitless, so it is impossible to know their rulings individually one by one because of...
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the definition of fiqh, focusing on whether necessary religious knowledge (daruriyyat al-din) should be excluded from its definition. The commentary opens by addressing an earlier point about adding 'amaliyya (practical) to Abu Hanifa's definition to exclude ethics. The main debate involves the matn (Sadr al-Shariah, a Hanafi) and the sharh (al-Taftazani, a Shafi'i). The matn objects to Imam al-Razi's condition in al-Mahsul that fiqh only applies to rulings not known necessarily from religion. The matn argues that this condition is superfluous because fiqh is a faculty (malaka) that requires ijtihad; even knowing many issues does not make one a faqih without this faculty, let alone knowing one necessary issue. Therefore, no condition is needed to exclude them. Taftazani responds that Imam al-Razi's condition is not restrictive but clarificatory: it simply states the Shafi'i position that fiqh is about non-evident, deductive rulings. It does not aim to prevent necessary knowledge from being included—since that is already excluded by the requirement of deduction. Thus the condition is not wasted. The passage then begins a new objection about the term 'ahkam' (rulings) in the definition, questioning whether it means all, some, or a proportion. This second objection is cut off mid-sentence. The commentary thus highlights a key usul dispute: whether the definition of fiqh should explicitly exclude necessary knowledge, and whether fiqh is a collection of knowledge or a faculty.

Key Terms
فقه (fiqh): Knowledge of practical shar'i rulings obtained through deduction (istidlal) and not from necessary religious knowledge.
ضروريات الدين (daruriyyat al-din): Matters of religion known by necessity, such as obligation of prayer, fasting, etc.
استدلال (istidlal): Deduction from evidence; the method by which fiqh is acquired.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this lesson, why is Imam al-Razi's condition excluding necessary religious knowledge considered redundant?
A) Because necessary knowledge is impossible to acquire.
B) Because fiqh is defined as a faculty of deduction, so necessary knowledge (which requires no deduction) is automatically excluded.
C) Because the condition is actually harmful to the definition.
D) Because the Shafi'i school does not accept it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view holds that fiqh is a faculty of deduction, making a separate exclusion of necessary knowledge redundant; the Shafi'i view adds the condition for clarity, but both agree that knowing only necessary rulings does not make one a faqih.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
6 min
Defining Fiqh: Is it the Faculty or the Act of Knowing?
Definitional debate on fiqh with four refutations and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi usul defines fiqh as a malaka (faculty) and evaluate the four refutations against Ibn Hajib's definition of al-tahayyu' al-qareeb.

Core Idea
Fiqh is a faculty (malaka) to derive rulings, not the sum of known rulings.

In this passage, the author challenges Ibn Hajib's definition of fiqh as 'near ability' (al-tahayyu' al-qareeb) through four critiques. The commentator then defends Ibn Hajib, arguing that the ability to derive rulings is itself the knowledge that matters. This debate clarifies a core Hanafi usul position: fiqh is a faculty (malaka) that empowers the mujtahid to derive rulings, not merely a collection of known verdicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rival definitions
Ibn Hajib defines fiqh as al-tahayyu' al-qareeb (near ability); the author implies it should be actual knowledge of all rulings.
2
Trace the author's four refutations
List each argument: (1) it would require knowing all rulings, (2) it would preclude mistakes, (3) some issues have no ijtihad scope, (4) using 'ilm without a qualifier is insufficient.
These are directed against Ibn Hajib's definition.
3
Follow the commentator's responses
Examine the rebuttals: errors come from obstacles (e.g., headache, confusion), the hadith of Mu'adh proves ijtihad in all non-textual cases, and 'ilm in definitions means malaka not actual knowledge.
The commentator defends Ibn Hajib's definition as valid.
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
A person with a few rulings is not a faqih if lacking malaka; a mujtahid with malaka is a faqih even before knowing every ruling.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
Fiqh is a malaka, and the definition is accepted as standard in the Hanafi school.
This aligns with the commentator's defense.

جواب دیا کہ ہم احکام سے مراد مجموعہ کل احکام مراد لیتے ہیں، باقی رہا کہ کل مجموعہ احکام تو کسی کو معلوم نہیں ہو سکتے تو انہوں نے کہا کہ ہم علم بالا حکام سے معلوم کرنے کی استعداد اور صلاحیت مراد لیتے ہیں تو مصنف نے ابن حاجب کا رد کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر آپ تھیو سے استعداد بعیدہ مراد لیتے ہیں وہ تو ہر شخص کے اندر موجود ہے پھر تو ہر شخص کا فقیہ مجتہد ہونا لازم آتا ہے اور اگر استعداد قریبہ مراد لیتے کو ماخذ ( قرآن حدیث ) معلوم ہو اور اجتہاد کے لیے ضروری اسباب وشرائط مثلا قوائد صرفیه و نحویہ حاصل ہوں تو ایسا شخص بوقت ضرورت ہر آنے والے حادثے اور واقعہ کا حکم بذریعہ اجتہاد اپنی خداداد صلاحیت کے معلوم کر سکے اردو ہماری مراد تھیں قریب سے اس قسم کی صلاحیت مراد ہے تو مصنف نے اس کا چار وجوہ سے رد کیا ہے اگر تھیو مذکور کافی ہوتا تو ہر ایک مجتہد کو ہر مسئلہ معلوم ہوتا حالانکہ امام ابو حنیفہ جیسے ،تعریفات میں لفظ "علم" بول کر اس قسم کا تصیر مخصوص مراد لینا جس کے لیے کوئی قرینہ نہ ہو درست نہیں۔ قال الشارح: " يمكن الجواب عنها بأنا لا نسلم أن عدم تيسر معرفة بعض الأحكام لبعض الفقهاء أو الخطأ ينافي التهيؤ بالمعنى المذكور ، لجواز أن يكون ذلك بتعارض الأدلة ، أو وجود المانع ، أو معارضة الوهم للعقل ، أو مشاكلته الحق الباطل ، ونحو ذلك ولا نسلم أن شيئا من الأحكام التي لم يرد بها نص ولا إجماع يكون بحيث لا مساغ فيه للاجتهاد ، يدل عليه حديث معاذ رضى الله عنه حيث اعتمد على الاجتهاد برأيه فيما لا يجد فيه النص ، ولم يقل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فإن لم يكن حملا للاجتهاد، ولا نسلم لا دلالة للفظ العلم على التهيؤ المخصوص فإن معناه : ملكة يقتدر بها على إدراك جزئيات الأحكام ، وإطلاق العلم عليها شائع ذائع في العرف كقولهم في تعريف العلوم علم كذا وكذا فإن المحققين على أن المراد به هذه الملكة ويقال لها : الصناعة أيضا ، لا نفس الإدراك، وكقولهم : وجه الشبه بين العلم والحيوة كونهما جهتي إدراك . تشریح يہاں سے شارح مذکورہ چاروں اعتراضات کا جواب دینا چاہتے ہیں۔ حاصل یہ کہ اگر کسی مجتہد کو تعارض ادلہ کی وجہ سے یا موائعات موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے، مثلا: سر درد وغیرہ کے اجتہاد نہ ہو سکے تو یہ تهی مخصوص کے منافی نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر معارضہ وہم یا کی وجہ سے حق و باطل کے اشتباہ کی وجہ سے کسی مسئلے میں غلطی واقع ہو جائے تو تھی مخصوص کے منافی نہیں، اسی طرح یہ بھی ہم تسلیم کرنے کے لیے تیار نہیں کہ جس حکم میں قرآن و حدیث سے کوئی نص موجود نہ ہو اس میں اجتہاد کی گنجائش نہیں ہوتی اگر ایسی بات ہوتی تو حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم حضرت معاذ کو جب یمن کی طرف بھیج رہے تھے اور فرمایا کہ اے معاذ! اگر آپ کو قرآن وحدیث سے مسئلہ نہ مل سکے تو کیا کرو گے؟ تو کہا کہ أجتهد برأیی تو یہاں پر آپ خاموش ہو گئے وگرنہ آپ فرماتے إن لم تجد محلا و مساغا للاجتهاد ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ ہر وہ حکم جو قرآن و حدیث میں منصوص نہ ہو اس میں اجتہاد ہو سکتا ہے۔ باقی مصنف کا کہنا کہ علم بول کر تھیو اور ملکہ مراد لینا صحیح نہیں ہے یہ بات بھی صحیح نہیں اور علم بمعنی ملکہ کے علوم کی تعریفات میں عام ہے چنانچہ محققین فرماتے ہیں کہ جہاں پر کسی علم کی تعریف کرتے ہوئے کہا جاتا ہے علم کذا، مثلا علم نحو هو علم بأصول يعرف بها أحوال... إلخ تو اس سے مراد ملکہ ہے جس کو یہ لوگ صناعت بھی کہتے ہیں نہ کہ علم و ادراک مراد ہے اسی طرح یہ جو کہا جاتا ہے کہ عالم حی کی مثل ہے اور جاہل مردہ کی مثل ہے، یا علم حیات کی مثل ہے اور جہل موت کی مثل ہے تو علم بمعنی ملکہ کے ہے کیونکہ علم اور حیات کے درمیان جو وجہ تشبیہ بیان کی جاتی ہے وہ كونهما جهتي إدراك تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے جیسے کہ علم بمعنی ملکہ و ذریعہ ادراک ہے اسی طرح حیات بھی وسیله و ذریعہ ادراک ہے تو ظاہر ہے کہ یہاں علم بمعنی ملکہ کے ہے اور اگر علم بمعنی و ادراک وجانے کے کہو تو کلام بہمل ہو جاتا ہے۔
قال الشارح : " قوله : بل هو تعريف مخترع للفقه بحيث ينضبط معلوماته والتقييد بكل الأحكام يخرج به البعض إلا أنه يدل على أنه إذ ظهر نزول الوحي بحكم أو حكمين فالعالم به مع الملكة المذكورة لا يسمى فقيها وإذا علم ثلثة أحكام يسمى فقيها . وقيد نزو
He answered: We intend by 'rulings' the total collection of rulings. As for the fact that the total collection cannot be known by anyone, they said: We intend by 'knowledge of rulings' the ability and capacity to know them. So the author, refuting Ibn Hajib, said: If you intend by 'al-tahayyu'' the distant ability, then that exists in every person, and thus every person would have to be a faqih mujtahid. And if you intend the near ability, then there is no universal rule for how much ability is called 'al-tahayyu' al-qareeb'. In any case, it is an ambiguous matter. Then Ibn Hajib replied: We intend by 'al-tahayyu'' the near ability, whose definition is that a person knows the sources (Qur'an and Hadith) and possesses the necessary means and conditions for ijtihad, such as rules of morphology and syntax. Then such a person, at the time of need, can know the ruling of every occurring event through ijtihad by his God-given ability. In Urdu, we intend by 'al-tahayyu' al-qareeb' this kind of ability. So the author refuted this with four points: If the mentioned ability sufficed, then every mujtahid would know every issue, whereas a personality like Imam Abu Hanifa could not know the meaning of 'dahr' (what period of time it denotes). If the mentioned ability sufficed, then no mujtahid would ever make a mistake. There are some events and occurrences in which there is no scope for ijtihad. In definitions, using the word 'ilm' to intend this specific kind without any contextual indicator is not correct. The commentator said: 'It can be answered that we do not accept that the difficulty of knowing some rulings for some jurists or error contradicts al-tahayyu' in the mentioned sense, because that could be due to conflicting evidences, or the presence of an obstacle, or the mind's imagination opposing reason, or truth being confused with falsehood, etc. And we do not accept that any ruling for which there is neither text nor consensus is such that there is no scope for ijtihad regarding it; the hadith of Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him) indicates this, as he relied on ijtihad by his opinion regarding what he did not find a text for, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not say, 'If you do not find a place for ijtihad...' And we do not accept that the word 'ilm' does not indicate the specific al-tahayyu', for its meaning is a faculty by which one is able to comprehend particulars of rulings, and applying 'ilm' to it is widespread in usage, as their saying in defining sciences: 'the science of such-and-such', for the verifiers are of the view that what is meant is this faculty, also called 'the craft', not comprehension itself, and as their saying: 'The point of similarity between knowledge and life is that both are instruments of comprehension.' Commentary: From here the commentator intends to answer the four objections. The summary is that if a mujtahid cannot perform ijtihad due to conflicting evidences or existing obstacles such as headache etc., this does not contradict the specific al-tahayyu'. Similarly, if due to the imagination opposing reason or confusion of truth and falsehood an error occurs in an issue, that does not contradict the specific al-tahayyu'. Similarly, we are not prepared to accept that a ruling for which no text exists in Qur'an and Hadith has no scope for ijtihad. If that were the case, then when the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent Mu'adh to Yemen and asked: 'O Mu'adh! If you cannot find an issue in Qur'an and Hadith, what will you do?' He said: 'I will exercise ijtihad based on my opinion.' Then the Prophet remained silent; otherwise he would have said: 'If you do not find a place for ijtihad.' So it is known that every ruling not explicitly mentioned in Qur'an and Hadith can be subject to ijtihad. As for the author's statement that using 'ilm' to intend al-tahayyu' and malaka is not correct, that too is not correct; 'ilm' in the sense of malaka is common in definitions of sciences. Indeed, the verifiers say that when they say in defining a science, 'the science of such-and-such', e.g., 'the science of grammar is a science by which...', what is meant is the malaka, which they also call 'craft', not knowledge and perception. Similarly, what is said: 'The scholar is like the living and the ignorant like the dead', or 'Knowledge is like life and ignorance is like death', here 'ilm' is in the sense of malaka because the point of similarity between knowledge and life that is mentioned is that both are instruments of comprehension. So its meaning is that knowledge is a malaka and a means of comprehension, just as life is a means and instrument of comprehension. It is clear that here 'ilm' is in the sense of malaka, and if you interpret 'ilm' as knowledge and perception, the speech becomes meaningless.'
The commentator said: 'His saying: Rather, it is an invented definition of fiqh such that its known matters are well-defined, and the restriction to 'all rulings' excludes some. However, it indicates that if revelation of a ruling or two appears, the one who knows it along with the mentioned malaka is not called a faqih, and when he knows three rulings he is called a faqih. And the condition "nuzūl"...'
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
Passage type: Definitional debate in usul al-fiqh. The text presents Ibn Hajib's definition of fiqh as 'al-tahayyu' al-qareeb' (near ability) to derive rulings from sources, followed by the author's (likely from al-Tawdih) four refutations, and then the commentator's (al-Talwih) defense of Ibn Hajib. The author argues that if al-tahayyu' is taken as distant ability (present in all), everyone becomes a mujtahid; if near ability, it lacks a criterion. He provides four specific criticisms: (1) it would require a mujtahid to know all rulings, but even Abu Hanifa did not know the precise meaning of 'dahr'; (2) it would prevent errors, but mujtahids err; (3) some issues have no scope for ijtihad; (4) using the word 'ilm' without a qualifier for a specific meaning is invalid. The commentator refutes these: (1) it is not contradictory; errors may arise from conflicting evidences, obstacles (e.g., headache), or confusion; (2) the hadith of Mu'adh proves that ijtihad is permissible in all non-textual matters; (3) 'ilm' is commonly used in definitions of sciences to mean 'malaka' (faculty), not actual knowledge, as in 'ilm al-nahw' and analogies with life. He upholds Ibn Hajib's definition. This reflects the Hanafi usul school's emphasis on ijtihad and the faculty-based definition of fiqh.

Key Terms
التهيؤ (al-tahayyu'): The ability or preparedness to derive rulings from legal sources, specifically the 'near ability' that requires knowledge of sources and tools of ijtihad.
الملكة (al-malaka): A firmly established faculty in the soul by which one can derive rulings; synonymous with 'al-tahayyu' al-qareeb'.
العلم (al-‘ilm): In the context of definitions of sciences, it means malaka (faculty), not mere perception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does the author's claim that Ibn Hajib's definition lacks a universal criterion fail?
A) Because the definition includes all necessary tools
B) Because near ability is defined as knowledge of sources and tools of ijtihad
C) Because the author's own definition is worse
D) Because the commentator rejected the author's objection entirely

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is a faculty (malaka) to derive rulings from detailed sources, not merely a collection of known rulings.

Hanafi Definition of Fiqh: Conditions and Madhhab Dispute
Expanding the Hanafi definition of fiqh with conditions and madhhab critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh, identify its four conditions, and explain the practical difference with the Shafi'i definition.

Core Idea
Fiqh requires both knowledge of revealed rulings and the faculty (malaka) to derive new ones – three rulings plus malaka make a faqih.

In this passage, the commentator presents the Hanafi definition of fiqh in response to the Shafi'i definition. The author introduces critical conditions: the rulings must have appeared (zuhur), be at least three in number, and the jurist must possess malakat al-istinbat—the ability to derive subsidiary rulings from evidences. This definition transforms fiqh from scattered knowledge into a systematic, certain science. Let's unpack each condition step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its components
Locate the author's definition: 'knowledge of all practical Shari'i rulings concerning which the descent of revelation has appeared and concerning which consensus has been reached, from their evidences, together with the ability to correctly derive from them.' Note the four key elements: (1) all ahkam (2) with zuhur (3) from evidences (4) with malaka.
The definition is contrasted with the Shafi'i view that fiqh is simply knowledge of rulings without malaka.
2
Understand the plural condition (at least three rulings)
The word 'ahkam' is plural; in Arabic usage, the minimum for a plural is three. Thus, a person who knows only one or two rulings (with malaka) is not called a faqih. Knowledge of three rulings (with malaka) qualifies one as a faqih.
This is a strict linguistic requirement—not a subjective judgment.
3
Understand the zuhur condition (appearance of rulings)
The author restricts 'nuzul' with 'zuhur'. A ruling may have been revealed but not yet reached the jurist. It is not required for the jurist to know such rulings; his fiqh is not diminished by ignorance of unrevealed or uncommunicated rulings.
This prevents unfair judgment of a jurist who lacks access to newly revealed texts.
4
Analyze malakat al-istinbat (the reasoning faculty)
Two interpretations are given: (a) the ability to derive subsidiary analogical rulings from the known rulings, or (b) the ability to derive rulings directly from their evidences. Both require active juristic reasoning, not passive memorization. Without this malaka, one is not a faqih even if he knows many texts.
This is the core innovation of the Hanafi definition—fiqh is an active, productive science.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i definition
The Shafi'i definition (as characterized here) defines fiqh as knowledge of scattered rulings without requiring malaka. The Hanafi definition makes fiqh 'regulated and certain' (mundabit wa qat'i). The practical difference: a person who knows many rulings but cannot derive new ones is a faqih for Shafi'is but not for Hanafis.
This difference impacts who qualifies as a mujtahid and the methodology of ifta'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : " قوله : بل هو تعريف مخترع للفقه بحيث ينضبط معلوماته والتقييد بكل الأحكام يخرج به البعض إلا أنه يدل على أنه إذ ظهر نزول الوحي بحكم أو حكمين فالعالم به مع الملكة المذكورة لا يسمى فقيها وإذا علم ثلثة أحكام يسمى فقيها . وقيد نزول الوحى بالظهور" احتراز عما إذا نزل به الوحى و لم يبلغ بعد فليس من شرط الفقيه معرفته. تشريح
متن نے شوافع کی تعریف کو مخدوش ٹھہرانے کے بعد اپنی طرف سے تعریف کی ہے هـو الـعـلـم بكل الأحكام الشرعيه العمليه التي قد ظهر نزول الوحى بها والتي انعقد الإجماع عليها من أدلتها مع ملكة الاستنباط الصحيح منها يعنی ان تمام احکام کو جاننا جن کے متعلق وحی کا نزول ظاہر ہو چکا، یا اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے اور باقی احکام کے استنباط کا ملکہ موجود ہو ۔ اب اس تعریف سے فقہ ایک منضبط اور قطعی علم ہو گیا بخلاف شوافع کی تعریف کے اس میں فقہ علم بالا حکام کا نام تھا جو کہ مہم اور غیر معین تھے پھر مصنف کی تعریف میں "بكل الأحکام" کی قید لگا کر بعض احکام کو خارج کر دیا کہ بعض احکام کے جانے کو فقہ نہیں کہا جائے گا ہاں اگر ابھی تک کل احکام ایک یا دو کا نزول ہوا ہے اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا، کیونکہ احکام جمع ہے اور جمع کے کم از کم تین افراد ہوتے ہیں تو تین احکام کے جاننے کے بعد ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ فقیہ کہلائے گا، پھر نزول کو ظہور" کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اسلیے کہ صرف احکام کا نزول کافی نہیں بلکہ فقیہ تک ان کا ظہور اور پہنچنا بھی ضروری ہے لہذا اگر احکام تو نازل ہو چکے ہیں مگر فقیہ کے پاس ان کا ظہور نہیں ہوا تو فقیہ کے لیے ان کا جاننا ضروری نہیں اور ان کے نہ جاننے سے اس کی فقاہت پر کوئی اثر نہ ہوگا۔
قال الشارح : " قوله " مع ملكة الاستنباط “ أى : العلم بماذكر يشترط كونه مقرونا بملكة الاستنباط الفرعيه القياسيه من تلك الأحكام أو استنباط الأحكام من أدلتها حتى أن العلم بمجرد سماع النص للعلم باللغة من غير اقتدار على النظر والاستدلال لا يعد من الفقه والأول أوجه " .
تشريح
یہاں ماتن نے جو فقہ کی تعریف میں مع ملكة الاستنباط کے الفاظ استعمال کیسے ہے اس کی دو تو جیہیں کرنا چاہتے ہیں ”الاستنباط “ کی الف لام مضاف الیہ کے عوض ہے اگر مضاف الیہ مسائل قیاسیہ کو بنایا جائے تو مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ مجتہد کو علم بالوحی کے ساتھ ساتھ ان احکام سے مسائل قیاسیہ کے استنباط کا ملکہ ہو۔
The commentator said: 'His statement: Rather it is an invented definition of fiqh such that its objects of knowledge are regulated, and the restriction to 'all ahkam' excludes some, but it indicates that when revelation has appeared concerning one or two rulings, the one who knows them with the aforementioned malaka is not called a faqih, and when he knows three rulings he is called a faqih. And he restricted 'the descent of revelation' with 'appearance' as a safeguard against when revelation descended but has not yet reached him, so it is not a condition for the faqih to know it.' Commentary: After declaring the Shafi'i definition flawed, the author (matn) presented his own definition: 'It is knowledge of all the practical Shari'i rulings concerning which the descent of revelation has appeared and concerning which consensus has been reached, from their evidences, together with the ability (malaka) to correctly derive from them.' That is, to know all the rulings regarding which the revelation has become apparent or on which consensus has been established, and to possess the ability to derive the remaining rulings. With this definition, fiqh becomes a regulated and definitive science, unlike the Shafi'i definition where fiqh was knowledge of scattered rulings, indefinite. Then, by restricting with 'all ahkam' in the author's definition, he excludes some rulings: knowing only some rulings is not called fiqh. If only one or two rulings have been revealed so far, the one who knows them is not called a faqih, because 'ahkam' is a plural and a plural minimally indicates three. So after knowing three rulings together with the ability to derive, he is called a faqih. Then he restricted 'nuzul' with 'zuhur' because mere descent of rulings is not enough; their appearance and reaching the faqih is also necessary. If rulings have descended but have not appeared to the faqih, it is not necessary for him to know them, and his not knowing them does not affect his fiqh. The commentator said: 'His statement "with malakat al-istinbat" means: knowledge of what was mentioned must be accompanied by the ability to derive subsidiary analogical matters from those rulings or to derive rulings from their evidences, such that mere hearing the text with linguistic knowledge without ability to consider and infer is not considered fiqh; the first is more appropriate.' Commentary: Here the author's use of 'with malakat al-istinbat' in the definition of fiqh is given two interpretations. The 'al' in 'al-istinbat' substitutes for the possessive; if the possessive is taken to be 'analogical matters', the meaning is that the mujtahid must have, along with knowledge of the revelation, the ability to derive analogical matters from those rulings.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion. The author (matn) responds to the Shafi'i definition of fiqh and presents his own Hanafi definition. The core of the definition is: 'knowledge of all practical Shari'i rulings from their detailed evidences' (as per the well-known definition), but here he includes the condition 'the descent of revelation has appeared' (zahara nuzul al-wahi) and 'consensus has been reached' (in'aqada al-ijma'), plus 'with malakat al-istinbat' (ability to derive). The passage explains three key points: 1) The plural 'ahkam' requires at least three rulings to be known before one qualifies as a faqih. 2) 'Appearance' (zuhur) means the ruling must have reached the jurist; mere revelation is not enough. 3) 'Malakat al-istinbat' ensures that mere memory of texts without reasoning ability does not constitute fiqh. The commentator (sharih) provides two interpretations: either the malaka is the ability to derive subsidiary rulings (furu') from the principles, or the ability to derive rulings directly from their evidences. Both require active juristic reasoning, not passive knowledge. This definition makes fiqh a systematic and certain science, contrasting with the Shafi'i view that it is knowledge of scattered ahkam. The Hanafi emphasis is on malaka (faculty) as essential for a faqih, which aligns with their usul methodology favoring istihsan and qiyas.

Key Terms
ملکة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): A firm faculty in the soul enabling the jurist to derive subsidiary rulings from the primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) using principles like qiyas.
الفقہ (al-fiqh): Knowledge (ilm) of all practical Shari'i rulings that have come via revelation or ijma, accompanied by the ability (malaka) to derive other rulings from their evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To emphasize that rulings must be from revelation.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in the Hanafi tradition is not just knowing rulings but possessing the faculty to derive new ones from the sources, with the added condition that the rulings must have been accessible to the jurist.

The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh: Precision and Discipline
Defining fiqh with precision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh and explain how it differs from the Shafi'i definition.

Core Idea
Fiqh is disciplined knowledge of all revealed and agreed rulings, coupled with the faculty of derivation.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of fiqh as presented in the commentary on al-Tawdih. The author contrasts it with the vague Shafi'i definition, emphasizing precision and certainty. We will explore the key components: all rulings, appearance of revelation, and the necessity of the faculty of derivation (malakat al-istinbat).

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition
Locate the Arabic text: هو العلم بكل الأحكام الشرعية العملية التي قد ظهر نزول الوحي بها والتي انعقد الإجماع عليها من أدلتها مع ملكة الاستنباط الصحيح منها. Write it down.
This is the full Hanafi definition.
2
Analyze each component
Break down the definition: (1) العلم بكل الأحكام — knowledge of all rulings (minimum three); (2) ظهر نزول الوحي — revelation must have appeared; (3) مع ملكة الاستنباط — accompanied by the faculty of correct derivation.
The term 'كل' (all) excludes knowing only one or two rulings.
3
Compare with Shafi'i definition
The passage states that the Shafi'i definition (علم بالأحكام) is vague and indeterminate (مهم وغير معين). Contrast: Hanafi definition is disciplined (منضبط) and certain (قطعي).
Shafi'i position: fiqh is mere knowledge of rulings, without requiring derivation faculty.
4
Apply the three-ruling minimum
The text notes that 'plural' requires at least three. Therefore, a person knowing one or two revealed rulings cannot be called a faqih unless they also possess malakat al-istinbat.
This shows the definition's precision: quantity matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوحى بالظهور" احتراز عما إذا نزل به الوحى و لم يبلغ بعد فليس من شرط الفقيه معرفته. تشريح ماتن نے شوافع کی تعریف کو مخدوش ٹھہرانے کے بعد اپنی طرف سے تعریف کی ہے هو العلم بكل الأحكام الشرعيه العمليه التي قد ظهر نزول الوحى بها والتي انعقد الإجماع عليها من أدلتها مع ملكة الاستنباط الصحيح منها يعنی ان تمام احکام کو جاننا جن کے متعلق وحی کا نزول ظاہر ہو چکا، یا اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے اور باقی احکام کے استنباط کا ملکہ موجود ہو ۔ اب اس تعریف سے فقہ ایک منضبط اور قطعی علم ہو گیا بخلاف شوافع کی تعریف کے اس میں فقہ علم بالا حکام کا نام تھا جو کہ مہم اور غیر معین تھے پھر مصنف کی تعریف میں "بكل الأحکام" کی قید لگا کر بعض احکام کو خارج کر دیا کہ بعض احکام کے جانے کو فقہ نہیں کہا جائے گا ہاں اگر ابھی تک کل احکام ایک یا دو کا نزول ہوا ہے اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا، کیونکہ احکام جمع ہے اور جمع کے کم از کم تین افراد ہوتے ہیں تو تین احکام کے جاننے کے بعد ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ فقیہ کہلائے گا، پھر نزول کو ظہور" کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اسلیے کہ صرف احکام کا نزول کافی نہیں بلکہ فقیہ تک ان کا ظہور اور پہنچنا بھی ضروری ہے لہذا اگر احکام تو نازل ہو چکے ہیں مگر فقیہ کے پاس ان کا ظہور نہیں ہوا تو فقیہ کے لیے ان کا جاننا ضروری نہیں اور ان کے نہ جاننے سے اس کی فقاہت پر کوئی اثر نہ ہوگا۔
قال الشارح : " قوله " مع ملكة الاستنباط " أى : العلم بماذكر يشترط كونه مقرونا بملكة الاستنباط الفروعيه القياسيه من تلك الأحكام أو استنباط الأحكام من أدلتها حتى أن العلم بمجرد سماع النص للعلم باللغة من غير اقتدار على النظر والاستدلال لا يعد من الفقه والأول أوجه " .
تشريح یہاں ماتن نے جو فقہ کی تعریف میں مع ملكة الاستنباط کے الفاظ استعمال کیسے ہے اس کی دو تو جیہیں کرنا چاہتے ہیں ”الاستنباط “ کی الف لام مضاف الیہ کے عوض ہے اگر مضاف الیہ مسائل قیاسیہ کو بنایا جائے تو مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ مجتہد کو علم بالوحی کے ساتھ ساتھ ان احکام سے مسائل قیاسیہ کے استنباط کا ملکہ بھی ہو ،، اگر مضاف الیہ احکام کو بنایا جائے تو مطلب یہ ہوگا علم بما نزل به الوحی وانعقد عليه الإجماع کے ساتھ ان احکام کو ان کے دلائل سے استنباط کرنے کا ملکہ بھی موجود ہو یعنی اگر ایک آدمی محض اپنی لغت دانی کی بنا پر احکام کو سمجھ سکتا ہے باقی اشارۃ النص یا اقتضاء النص سے حکم معلوم کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں تو اس کو مجتہد نہ کہا جائے گا مگر پہلی تو جیہ زیادہ ظاہر ہے کہ کیونکہ مجتہد اس کو کہا جاتا ہے جو احکام منصوصہ سے مسائل فرعیہ قیاسیہ مستنبط کر سکے ، مثلا شراب حرام ہے یہ حکم منصوص ہے اب جو اس سے بھنگ افیون کا حکم بھی معلوم کر ۔ اس کو فقیہ کہا جائے گا۔
قال الشارح : " قوله " لا المسائل القياسيه " أي : لا يشترط في الفقه بالعلم بالمسائل القياسيه لأنها نتيجة الفقاهة والاجتهاد ؛ لكونها فروعا مستنبطة بالاجتهاد فيتوقف العلم لها على كون الشخص فقيها فلو توقف الفقاهة عليها لزم الدور. فإن قيل : هذا إنما يستقيم في أول القائسين ، وأما بعده فيجوز أن يشترط فيه العلم بالمسائل القياسيه التي يستنبطها المجتهد الأول من غير دور . قلنا: لا يجوز للمجتهد التقليد بل يجب عليه أن يعرف المسائل القياسيه بالاجتهاده فلو اشترط العلم لزم الدور ـ نعم يشترط أن يعرف أقوال المجتهدين في المسائل القياسيه لئلا يقع في مخالفة الإجماع .
تشريح ماتن نے کہا کہ مجتہد کے لیے علم بمانزل به الوحی اور اجماعی مسائل کو جاننا ضروری ہے نہ کہ قیاسی مسائل کو ۔ اب شارح اس عدمی شرط کی وضاحت پیش کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ مجتہد کے لیے مسائل قیاسیہ کا جاننا شرط نہیں ، اس لیے کہ مسائل قیاسیہ خود اس مجتہد کی فقاہت کا نتیجہ ہیں اب اگر مجتہد کے فقیہ بننے کے لیے انہی مسائل کو جانا شرط کر دیا جائے تو دور لازم آئے گا۔ دور کا معنی ہے توقف الشئ علی ما يتوقف هو على ذلك الشئ تو مجتہد کی اپنی فقاہت اپنی فقاہت پر موقوف ہو جائے یہ دور ہے، جو کہ محال ہے۔
إن قبل ... الخ سے سوال نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں سوال یہ ہے کہ اول مجتہد میں آپ کی بات تو ٹھیک ہے کہ دور لازم آئے گا لیکن اگر بعد میں آنے والے مجتہد کے لیے پہلے مجتہد کے مسائل قیاسیہ
The revelation with appearance" is a precaution for when revelation has descended but has not yet reached; knowledge of it is not a condition for the faqih. Explanation: After the author criticized the Shafi'i definition, he defined from his own side: It is knowledge of all practical Shari'ah rulings regarding which the descent of revelation has appeared and on which consensus has been reached, from their evidences, along with the faculty of correct derivation from them. That is, knowing all those rulings concerning which the descent of revelation has become apparent or consensus has been concluded, and possessing the faculty to derive the remaining rulings. Now with this definition, fiqh becomes a disciplined and certain knowledge, unlike the Shafi'i definition in which fiqh was knowledge of rulings that were vague and indeterminate. Then in the author's definition, by restricting with 'all the rulings', some rulings are excluded: knowing some rulings will not be called fiqh. Yes, if only one or two rulings have descended so far, such a person will not be called a faqih because 'rulings' is plural and the minimum of plural is three, so after knowing three rulings along with the faculty of derivation, he will be called a faqih. Then he restricted 'descent' with 'appearance' because mere descent of rulings is not enough; rather, their appearance and reaching the faqih is also necessary. So if rulings have descended but their appearance has not reached the faqih, it is not necessary for him to know them, and not knowing them will not affect his fiqh. The commentator said: "His statement 'with the faculty of derivation' means: the knowledge of what was mentioned is conditional upon being accompanied by the faculty of deriving subsidiary analogical rulings from those rulings, or deriving rulings from their evidences, such that mere hearing the text due to knowledge of language without ability for consideration and inference is not considered fiqh, and the first is more apparent." Explanation: Here the author used the words 'with the faculty of derivation' in the definition of fiqh; he wants to give two interpretations. The 'al' and 'lam' of 'al-istinbat' is in place of the possessive construction. If the possessive is made to be 'qiyasi issues', then the meaning is: a mujtahid, along with knowledge of revelation, must also have the faculty of deriving qiyasi issues from those rulings. If the possessive is made to be 'rulings', then the meaning is: together with knowledge of what was revealed and consensus, there must also be the faculty of deriving those rulings from their evidences. That is, if a person can merely understand rulings based on his linguistic knowledge but does not have ability to derive rulings from 'isharat al-nass' or 'iqtida al-nass', he will not be called a mujtahid. However, the first interpretation is more apparent because a mujtahid is called one who can derive subsidiary analogical issues from textual rulings. For example, wine is forbidden; this is a textual ruling. Now one who can also derive the ruling of bhang [opium] from it will be called a faqih. The commentator said: "His statement 'not the qiyasi issues' means: knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition in fiqh because they are the result of fiqh and ijtihad; since they are subsidiary issues derived by ijtihad, knowledge of them depends on the person being a faqih. So if fiqh were dependent on them, circularity would result. If it is said: This only holds for the first of those who perform qiyas, but after him it is permissible to condition knowledge of the qiyasi issues that the first mujtahid derived without circularity. We say: It is not permissible for a mujtahid to do taqlid; rather, he must know the qiyasi issues through his own ijtihad. So if knowledge were conditioned, circularity would result. Yes, it is necessary that he know the sayings of the mujtahids concerning qiyasi issues to avoid contradicting consensus." Explanation: The author said that for a mujtahid, it is necessary to know the revealed and consensual issues, not the qiyasi issues. Now the commentator wants to clarify this negative condition: that knowing qiyasi issues is not a condition for a mujtahid, because qiyasi issues are themselves the result of the mujtahid's fiqh. If knowledge of these same issues is made a condition for a person to become a faqih, then circularity would result. Circularity means the dependence of a thing on what depends on that same thing, so the mujtahid's own fiqh would depend on his fiqh; this is circularity, which is impossible. From 'In qila...' etc., he conveys a question and answers it. The question is that your statement is correct regarding the first mujtahid that circularity would result, but for a later mujtahid, it is permissible to condition knowledge of the first mujtahid's qiyasi issues.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and commentary on the definition of fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) according to the Hanafi school. The author (mātn) first criticizes the Shāfiʿī definition of fiqh because it was vague and indeterminate, and then presents a precise definition: fiqh is knowledge of all practical Sharīʿah rulings that have been revealed (with evidence) and on which there is consensus, together with the faculty (malaka) of correct derivation (istinbāṭ) from those evidences. The passage then explains each part of the definition: 

- "All rulings" (bikull al-aḥkām): the term 'all' excludes knowing only a few rulings; one must know at least three rulings (the minimum of a plural) to be called a faqīh (jurist). 
- "Appearance of revelation" (ẓahara nuzūl al-waḥy): revelation must have reached the jurist; if rulings are revealed but not known to him, he is not required to know them. 
- "Along with the faculty of correct derivation" (maʿa malakat al-istinbāṭ aṣ-ṣaḥīḥ): this is the key condition that distinguishes a mujtahid from a mere narrator. The commentator gives two interpretations: (1) the faculty to derive analogical (qiyāsī) subsidiary issues from those rulings, or (2) the faculty to derive the rulings themselves from their evidences. The first interpretation is deemed stronger, as a mujtahid must be able to derive new rulings through qiyās, like extending the prohibition of wine to bhang. 

Then the passage discusses whether knowledge of qiyāsī issues is a condition for being a mujtahid. The author says it is not, because qiyāsī issues are the result of ijtihād. If knowing them were a condition, it would create a circular dependency (dawr): to be a mujtahid one would need knowledge that itself depends on being a mujtahid. However, a later mujtahid must know the rulings of earlier mujtahids to avoid violating consensus, but he does not need to know all qiyāsī issues in detail; he must derive them himself. 

Throughout, the passage maintains the Hanafi stress on ijtihād and the capacity for independent reasoning as essential for fiqh.

Key Terms
الفقہ (al-fiqh): العلم بكل الأحكام الشرعية العملية التي ظهر نزول الوحي بها وانعقد الإجماع عليها من أدلتها مع ملكة الاستنباط الصحيح منها
ملكة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): قوة و قدرة على استخراج الأحكام الفرعية القياسية من الأحكام المنصوصة أو استنباط الأحكام من أدلتها
مسائل قياسية (masā'il qiyāsiyya): الأحكام المستنبطة عن طريق القياس من الأحكام المنصوصة
ظهور (zuhur): ظهور نزول الوحي وبلوغه إلى الفقيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of revealed rulings a person must know (along with malakat al-istinbat) to be called a faqih according to the Hanafi definition in this passage?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh includes both knowledge of rulings and the capacity to derive new rulings, making it a rigorous and disciplined science.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Malakat al-Istinbat: The Faculty of Derivation
Explaining malakat al-istinbat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two interpretations of malakat al-istinbat and identify which one the commentator prefers, with an example.

Core Idea
The faculty of derivation is essential for ijtihad; it distinguishes a faqih from a mere narrator.

This lesson focuses on the key condition in the Hanafi definition: the faculty of correct derivation (malakat al-istinbat). The passage provides two ways to interpret this faculty and illustrates its importance through the example of deriving the ruling of bhang from the prohibition of wine. Understanding this faculty is crucial for grasping the Hanafi concept of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Locate the discussion of malakat al-istinbat
Find the sentence: 'قال الشارح : " قوله " مع ملكة الاستنباط " أى : العلم بماذكر يشترط كونه مقرونا بملكة الاستنباط الفروعيه القياسيه من تلك الأحكام أو استنباط الأحكام من أدلتها'.
This is where the commentator explains the phrase.
2
Understand the two interpretations
Interpretation 1: the faculty to derive qiyasi (analogical) subsidiary issues from those rulings. Interpretation 2: the faculty to derive the rulings themselves from their evidences (i.e., general istinbat).
The difference is whether the object of derivation is new rulings (qiyasi) or the original rulings (from evidences).
3
Note the commentator's preference
The commentator says 'والأول أوجه' — the first interpretation is more apparent. Reason: a mujtahid is called one who can derive subsidiary analogical issues from textual rulings.
The passage provides an example: from the prohibition of wine, derive the ruling of bhang (opium) via qiyas.
4
Apply the example
Wine (khamr) is prohibited by text. Using the faculty, one can analogize bhang (bang) to wine due to the shared illa of intoxication, deriving its prohibition.
This shows malakat al-istinbat in action: the ability to extend rulings to new cases.

الوحى بالظهور" احتراز عما إذا نزل به الوحى و لم يبلغ بعد فليس من شرط الفقيه معرفته. تشريح ماتن نے شوافع کی تعریف کو مخدوش ٹھہرانے کے بعد اپنی طرف سے تعریف کی ہے هو العلم بكل الأحكام الشرعيه العمليه التي قد ظهر نزول الوحى بها والتي انعقد الإجماع عليها من أدلتها مع ملكة الاستنباط الصحيح منها يعنی ان تمام احکام کو جاننا جن کے متعلق وحی کا نزول ظاہر ہو چکا، یا اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے اور باقی احکام کے استنباط کا ملکہ موجود ہو ۔ اب اس تعریف سے فقہ ایک منضبط اور قطعی علم ہو گیا بخلاف شوافع کی تعریف کے اس میں فقہ علم بالا حکام کا نام تھا جو کہ مہم اور غیر معین تھے پھر مصنف کی تعریف میں "بكل الأحکام" کی قید لگا کر بعض احکام کو خارج کر دیا کہ بعض احکام کے جانے کو فقہ نہیں کہا جائے گا ہاں اگر ابھی تک کل احکام ایک یا دو کا نزول ہوا ہے اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا، کیونکہ احکام جمع ہے اور جمع کے کم از کم تین افراد ہوتے ہیں تو تین احکام کے جاننے کے بعد ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ فقیہ کہلائے گا، پھر نزول کو ظہور" کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اسلیے کہ صرف احکام کا نزول کافی نہیں بلکہ فقیہ تک ان کا ظہور اور پہنچنا بھی ضروری ہے لہذا اگر احکام تو نازل ہو چکے ہیں مگر فقیہ کے پاس ان کا ظہور نہیں ہوا تو فقیہ کے لیے ان کا جاننا ضروری نہیں اور ان کے نہ جاننے سے اس کی فقاہت پر کوئی اثر نہ ہوگا۔

If the possessive is made to be 'qiyasi issues', then the meaning is: a mujtahid, along with knowledge of revelation, must also have the faculty of deriving qiyasi issues from those rulings. If the possessive is made to be 'rulings', then the meaning is: together with knowledge of what was revealed and consensus, there must also be the faculty of deriving those rulings from their evidences. That is, if a person can merely understand rulings based on his linguistic knowledge but does not have ability to derive rulings from 'isharat al-nass' or 'iqtida al-nass', he will not be called a mujtahid. However, the first interpretation is more apparent because a mujtahid is called one who can derive subsidiary analogical issues from textual rulings. For example, wine is forbidden; this is a textual ruling. Now one who can also derive the ruling of bhang [opium] from it will be called a faqih. The commentator said: "His statement 'not the qiyasi issues' means: knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition in fiqh because they are the result of fiqh and ijtihad; since they are subsidiary issues derived by ijtihad, knowledge of them depends on the person being a faqih. So if fiqh were dependent on them, circularity would result. If it is said: This only holds for the first of those who perform qiyas, but after him it is permissible to condition knowledge of the qiyasi issues that the first mujtahid derived without circularity. We say: It is not permissible for a mujtahid to do taqlid; rather, he must know the qiyasi issues through his own ijtihad. So if knowledge were conditioned, circularity would result. Yes, it is necessary that he know the sayings of the mujtahids concerning qiyasi issues to avoid contradicting consensus." Explanation: The author said that for a mujtahid, it is necessary to know the revealed and consensual issues, not the qiyasi issues. Now the commentator wants to clarify this negative condition: that knowing qiyasi issues is not a condition for a mujtahid, because qiyasi issues are themselves the result of the mujtahid's fiqh. If knowledge of these same issues is made a condition for a person to become a faqih, then circularity would result. Circularity means the dependence of a thing on what depends on that same thing, so the mujtahid's own fiqh would depend on his fiqh; this is circularity, which is impossible. From 'In qila...' etc., he conveys a question and answers it. The question is that your statement is correct regarding the first mujtahid that circularity would result, but for a later mujtahid, it is permissible to condition knowledge of the first mujtahid's qiyasi issues.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and commentary on the definition of fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) according to the Hanafi school. The author (mātn) first criticizes the Shāfiʿī definition of fiqh because it was vague and indeterminate, and then presents a precise definition: fiqh is knowledge of all practical Sharīʿah rulings that have been revealed (with evidence) and on which there is consensus, together with the faculty (malaka) of correct derivation (istinbāṭ) from those evidences. The passage then explains each part of the definition: 

- "All rulings" (bikull al-aḥkām): the term 'all' excludes knowing only a few rulings; one must know at least three rulings (the minimum of a plural) to be called a faqīh (jurist). 
- "Appearance of revelation" (ẓahara nuzūl al-waḥy): revelation must have reached the jurist; if rulings are revealed but not known to him, he is not required to know them. 
- "Along with the faculty of correct derivation" (maʿa malakat al-istinbāṭ aṣ-ṣaḥīḥ): this is the key condition that distinguishes a mujtahid from a mere narrator. The commentator gives two interpretations: (1) the faculty to derive analogical (qiyāsī) subsidiary issues from those rulings, or (2) the faculty to derive the rulings themselves from their evidences. The first interpretation is deemed stronger, as a mujtahid must be able to derive new rulings through qiyās, like extending the prohibition of wine to bhang. 

Then the passage discusses whether knowledge of qiyāsī issues is a condition for being a mujtahid. The author says it is not, because qiyāsī issues are the result of ijtihād. If knowing them were a condition, it would create a circular dependency (dawr): to be a mujtahid one would need knowledge that itself depends on being a mujtahid. However, a later mujtahid must know the rulings of earlier mujtahids to avoid violating consensus, but he does not need to know all qiyāsī issues in detail; he must derive them himself. 

Throughout, the passage maintains the Hanafi stress on ijtihād and the capacity for independent reasoning as essential for fiqh.

Key Terms
ملكة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): قوة و قدرة على استخراج الأحكام الفرعية القياسية من الأحكام المنصوصة أو استنباط الأحكام من أدلتها
مسائل قياسية (masā'il qiyāsiyya): الأحكام المستنبطة عن طريق القياس من الأحكام المنصوصة
شراب (khamr): الخمر (المسكر)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which interpretation of malakat al-istinbat does the commentator consider more apparent?
A) Deriving qiyasi subsidiary issues from textual rulings
B) Deriving rulings from their evidences
C) Both are equally valid
D) The second is more apparent

Key Takeaway
Malakat al-istinbat is the capacity to derive new rulings via qiyas, distinguishing a true faqih from a mere transmitter.

The Circularity of Conditioning Qiyasi Issues
Arguing against conditioning qiyasi issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition for fiqh and how the objection regarding later mujtahids is refuted.

Core Idea
Conditioning fiqh on knowledge of qiyasi issues creates an impossible circular dependency (dawr).

In this lesson, we examine a subtle point from the passage: why knowing the derived rulings (qiyasi issues) is not required for being a faqih. The commentator uses a logical argument to show that it would lead to circularity (dawr), and then addresses a potential objection about later mujtahids. This argument reinforces the definition of fiqh as requiring the faculty of derivation, not its products.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement
The passage says: 'لا المسائل القياسيه' — knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition in fiqh.
This is the negative condition being explained.
2
Understand the reasoning
Reason: qiyasi issues are the result (نتيجة) of fiqh and ijtihad. They are subsidiary issues derived by ijtihad. Therefore, knowledge of them depends on the person being a faqih first. If fiqh depended on them, it would be circular (دور).
Circularity: fiqh requires knowledge of qiyasi issues, but qiyasi issues require fiqh to derive them.
3
Analyze the objection
Objection: This reasoning only holds for the first mujtahid. For later mujtahids, they could learn the qiyasi issues from the first mujtahid, so no circularity.
The objection tries to avoid circularity by allowing later mujtahids to simply know existing rulings.
4
Follow the refutation
Refutation: A mujtahid cannot do taqlid; he must know qiyasi issues through his own ijtihad. Therefore, even for later mujtahids, conditioning knowledge would require them to already be mujtahids, causing circularity. However, they must know the rulings of earlier mujtahids to avoid violating consensus, but this does not make qiyasi issues a condition for fiqh.
The key: a mujtahid must derive himself; mere knowledge of others' rulings is not enough to be called a mujtahid.

قال الشارح : " قوله " مع ملكة الاستنباط " أى : العلم بماذكر يشترط كونه مقرونا بملكة الاستنباط الفروعيه القياسيه من تلك الأحكام أو استنباط الأحكام من أدلتها حتى أن العلم بمجرد سماع النص للعلم باللغة من غير اقتدار على النظر والاستدلال لا يعد من الفقه والأول أوجه " .
تشريح یہاں ماتن نے جو فقہ کی تعریف میں مع ملكة الاستنباط کے الفاظ استعمال کیسے ہے اس کی دو تو جیہیں کرنا چاہتے ہیں ”الاستنباط “ کی الف لام مضاف الیہ کے عوض ہے اگر مضاف الیہ مسائل قیاسیہ کو بنایا جائے تو مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ مجتہد کو علم بالوحی کے ساتھ ساتھ ان احکام سے مسائل قیاسیہ کے استنباط کا ملکہ بھی ہو ،، اگر مضاف الیہ احکام کو بنایا جائے تو مطلب یہ ہوگا علم بما نزل به الوحی وانعقد عليه الإجماع کے ساتھ ان احکام کو ان کے دلائل سے استنباط کرنے کا ملکہ بھی موجود ہو یعنی اگر ایک آدمی محض اپنی لغت دانی کی بنا پر احکام کو سمجھ سکتا ہے باقی اشارۃ النص یا اقتضاء النص سے حکم معلوم کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں تو اس کو مجتہد نہ کہا جائے گا مگر پہلی تو جیہ زیادہ ظاہر ہے کہ کیونکہ مجتہد اس کو کہا جاتا ہے جو احکام منصوصہ سے مسائل فرعیہ قیاسیہ مستنبط کر سکے ، مثلا شراب حرام ہے یہ حکم منصوص ہے اب جو اس سے بھنگ افیون کا حکم بھی معلوم کر ۔ اس کو فقیہ کہا جائے گا۔
قال الشارح : " قوله " لا المسائل القياسيه " أي : لا يشترط في الفقه بالعلم بالمسائل القياسيه لأنها نتيجة الفقاهة والاجتهاد ؛ لكونها فروعا مستنبطة بالاجتهاد فيتوقف العلم لها على كون الشخص فقيها فلو توقف الفقاهة عليها لزم الدور. فإن قيل : هذا إنما يستقيم في أول القائسين ، وأما بعده فيجوز أن يشترط فيه العلم بالمسائل القياسيه التي يستنبطها المجتهد الأول من غير دور . قلنا: لا يجوز للمجتهد التقليد بل يجب عليه أن يعرف المسائل القياسيه بالاجتهاده فلو اشترط العلم لزم الدور ـ نعم يشترط أن يعرف أقوال المجتهدين في المسائل القياسيه لئلا يقع في مخالفة الإجماع .

إن قبل ... الخ سے سوال نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں سوال یہ ہے کہ اول مجتہد میں آپ کی بات تو ٹھیک ہے کہ دور لازم آئے گا لیکن اگر بعد میں آنے والے مجتہد کے لیے پہلے مجتہد کے مسائل قیاسیہ
The revelation with appearance" is a precaution for when revelation has descended but has not yet reached; knowledge of it is not a condition for the faqih. Explanation: After the author criticized the Shafi'i definition, he defined from his own side: It is knowledge of all practical Shari'ah rulings regarding which the descent of revelation has appeared and on which consensus has been reached, from their evidences, along with the faculty of correct derivation from them. That is, knowing all those rulings concerning which the descent of revelation has become apparent or consensus has been concluded, and possessing the faculty to derive the remaining rulings. Now with this definition, fiqh becomes a disciplined and certain knowledge, unlike the Shafi'i definition in which fiqh was knowledge of rulings that were vague and indeterminate. Then in the author's definition, by restricting with 'all the rulings', some rulings are excluded: knowing some rulings will not be called fiqh. Yes, if only one or two rulings have descended so far, such a person will not be called a faqih because 'rulings' is plural and the minimum of plural is three, so after knowing three rulings along with the faculty of derivation, he will be called a faqih. Then he restricted 'descent' with 'appearance' because mere descent of rulings is not enough; rather, their appearance and reaching the faqih is also necessary. So if rulings have descended but their appearance has not reached the faqih, it is not necessary for him to know them, and not knowing them will not affect his fiqh. The commentator said: "His statement 'with the faculty of derivation' means: the knowledge of what was mentioned is conditional upon being accompanied by the faculty of deriving subsidiary analogical rulings from those rulings, or deriving rulings from their evidences, such that mere hearing the text due to knowledge of language without ability for consideration and inference is not considered fiqh, and the first is more apparent." Commentary
This passage is a definition and commentary on the definition of fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) according to the Hanafi school. The author (mātn) first criticizes the Shāfiʿī definition of fiqh because it was vague and indeterminate, and then presents a precise definition: fiqh is knowledge of all practical Sharīʿah rulings that have been revealed (with evidence) and on which there is consensus, together with the faculty (malaka) of correct derivation (istinbāṭ) from those evidences. The passage then explains each part of the definition: 

- "All rulings" (bikull al-aḥkām): the term 'all' excludes knowing only a few rulings; one must know at least three rulings (the minimum of a plural) to be called a faqīh (jurist). 
- "Appearance of revelation" (ẓahara nuzūl al-waḥy): revelation must have reached the jurist; if rulings are revealed but not known to him, he is not required to know them. 
- "Along with the faculty of correct derivation" (maʿa malakat al-istinbāṭ aṣ-ṣaḥīḥ): this is the key condition that distinguishes a mujtahid from a mere narrator. The commentator gives two interpretations: (1) the faculty to derive analogical (qiyāsī) subsidiary issues from those rulings, or (2) the faculty to derive the rulings themselves from their evidences. The first interpretation is deemed stronger, as a mujtahid must be able to derive new rulings through qiyās, like extending the prohibition of wine to bhang. 

Then the passage discusses whether knowledge of qiyāsī issues is a condition for being a mujtahid. The author says it is not, because qiyāsī issues are the result of ijtihād. If knowing them were a condition, it would create a circular dependency (dawr): to be a mujtahid one would need knowledge that itself depends on being a mujtahid. However, a later mujtahid must know the rulings of earlier mujtahids to avoid violating consensus, but he does not need to know all qiyāsī issues in detail; he must derive them himself. 

Throughout, the passage maintains the Hanafi stress on ijtihād and the capacity for independent reasoning as essential for fiqh.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): توقف الشيء على ما يتوقف هو على ذلك الشيء
مسائل قياسية (masā'il qiyāsiyya): الأحكام المستنبطة عن طريق القياس من الأحكام المنصوصة
تقليد (taqlid): اتباع قول الغير من غير دليل
إجماع (ijma): اتفاق المجتهدين على حكم شرعي

Checkpoint
What logical problem results from conditioning fiqh on knowledge of qiyasi issues?
A) A tautology
B) Circularity (dawr)
C) Infinite regress

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of derived rulings (qiyasi issues) results from fiqh, so it cannot be a prerequisite—this avoids the logical fallacy of dawr.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Objection of Variability in Defining Fiqh
First objection to the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first objection to the author's definition of fiqh and explain why it is considered problematic in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A definition that ties fiqh to ongoing revelation and consensus makes it fluctuate, contradicting its nature as a fixed science.

This lesson examines the first objection raised against the author's definition of fiqh. The author defined fiqh as 'knowledge of what has appeared by revelation or upon which consensus has been formed.' The objector argues that this definition makes fiqh a variable concept—increasing as new rulings are revealed or consensus formed, decreasing with abrogation—whereas fiqh, like other sciences (e.g., nahw and sarf), should be a specific and stable discipline. Understanding this critique sharpens our ability to evaluate definitions in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's definition of fiqh
Locate the definition in the passage: 'knowledge of what has appeared by revelation or upon which consensus has been formed.' Note that it includes two sources: revelation (wahy) and consensus (ijma').
2
Understand the objector's claim about fiqh's nature
The objector asserts that fiqh, as a technical term, should be a 'makhsus' (specific) science, like nahw and sarf—fixed and well-defined. It should not be a concept that grows or shrinks.
3
Analyze how the definition leads to increase
As new rulings are revealed (during the Prophet's time) or as new consensus is formed, the object of knowledge (the 'what' of fiqh) expands, causing fiqh itself to 'increase' according to the definition.
4
Analyze how the definition leads to decrease
When consensus contradicts a khabar wahid or when abrogating verses (nasikh) appear, some previously known rulings become no longer part of the revealed/consensus body, causing fiqh to 'decrease.'
5
Recognize the tension with the concept of a 'science'
A science is expected to have a fixed subject matter. The objection reveals that this definition makes fiqh's scope change over time, which contradicts the stability expected of a technical discipline.
Later Hanafi scholars respond by refining the definition to resolve this tension.
