یہاں سے مصنف کی بیان کردہ تعریف پر چند اعتراضات کر رہے ہیں ۔ پہلا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ یہاں پر فقہ اصطلاحی کی تعریف کرنا مقصود ہے اور فقہاء کے نزدیک فقہ ایک علم مخصوص کا نام ہے، جس طرح کہ باقی علوم محو ، صرف وغیرہ ہیں حالانکہ مصنف کی تعریف سے تو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ فقہ کوئی مخصوص علم نہیں بلکہ گھٹنے بڑھنے والا مفہوم کی ہے، کیونکہ مصنف کے نزدیک فقہ علم بما ظهر نزول الوحی به أو انعقد عليه الإجماع كا نام ہے تو جیسے احکام کا نزول زیادہ ہوتا جائے گا یا اجماعات کا انعقاد ہوتا جائے گا، فقہ بھی بڑھتا جائے گا ۔ اسی طرح نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ تک بڑھتا رہے گا پھر خبر واحد کے خلاف اجماع ہونے اور نواسخ کے ظہور کے ساتھ کم ہوتا جائے گا۔
From here, he is raising several objections to the definition stated by the author. The first objection is that here the intended purpose is to define technical fiqh, and according to jurists, fiqh is the name of a specific knowledge, just like other sciences such as syntax and morphology. However, from the author's definition, it appears that fiqh is not a specific knowledge but rather a concept that increases and decreases. Because according to the author, fiqh is the name of knowledge of what has appeared by the revelation of the revelation or upon which consensus has been formed. So as the revelation of rulings increases or the formation of consensus occurs, fiqh will increase. Similarly, it will keep increasing until the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and then it will decrease with the occurrence of consensus contrary to khabar al-wahid and the emergence of abrogators.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection to the author's definition of fiqh. The objector argues that fiqh, being a specific discipline like nahw and sarf, should be a fixed body of knowledge. But the author's definition—'knowledge of what has appeared by revelation or upon which consensus has been formed'—makes fiqh variable: it grows as new rulings are revealed or new consensus is formed, and it shrinks when consensus opposes a khabar wahid or abrogation occurs. This variability contradicts the nature of a defined science.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of what has appeared by revelation or upon which consensus has been formed (the criticized definition).
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the scholars of the ummah on a ruling.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith that does not reach tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first objection, why is the author's definition of fiqh problematic?
A) It includes only revealed rulings, excluding qiyas.
B) It makes fiqh a variable concept, not a fixed science.
C) It does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions.
D) It restricts fiqh to the time of revelation.

Key Takeaway
A definition of fiqh must avoid making it a variable concept, as fiqh is a specific discipline in usul al-fiqh.

Certainty of Fiqh Despite Zanni Means: Al-Razi's Argument
Explaining al-Razi's argument on certainty of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Hanafi usul establishes the certainty of fiqh rulings through ijma and tawatur ma'nawi, and apply the argument to distinguish between the ruling (qat'i) and its path (zanni).

Core Idea
The ruling is certain; the path is conjectural — ijma and tawatur ma'nawi transform zann into knowledge.

This passage presents the third response to the objection that fiqh cannot be called 'ilm because it relies on zanni evidence. Drawing on Imam al-Razi's argument from al-Mahsul, the response distinguishes between the ruling itself (qat'i) and the means of reaching it (zanni). The key move is that ijma and the abundance of ahadith on acting upon zann create a tawatur ma'nawi, making the obligation to act on the maznun ruling a qat'i principle. This lesson unpacks the reasoning across both taswib and takhti'a assumptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
State the main thesis: the ruling is qat'i, the path is zanni. The obligation to act on zann is established by definitive evidence.
This is the third response after two weaker ones.
2
Trace the dalil
Understand how ijma and tawatur ma'nawi prove that every maznun ruling is established in Allah's knowledge (on taswib).
Tawatur ma'nawi: different ahadith all point to the same meaning.
3
Distinguish the two assumptions
See how the argument works under taswib (every mujtahid correct) vs. takhti'a (only one correct). Under takhti'a, the certainty shifts to the obligation to act.
The Hanafi position generally aligns with taswib in furu'.
4
Examine the objection and rebuttal
The objection: maznun and ma'lum are opposites. Rebuttal: the maznun becomes ma'lum by considering the definitive proof that whatever is maznun for the mujtahid is established in reality (or its obligation is certain).
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
5
Synthesize the final refinement
Summarize the Sharh al-Minhaj refinement: every ruling wajib al-'amal qat'an is known qat'an to be Allah's ruling, so the maznun ruling is known qat'an. Fiqh is certain knowledge.
Zann is merely the epistemological means.

قال الشارح : " قوله : وثالثا : هو الذي ذكر في " المحصول “ وغيره أن الحكم مقطوع به والظن في طريقه . وتقريره : أنه لما دل الإجماع على وجوب العمل بالظن ، وكثرت أخبار الآحاد في ذلك ، حتى صارت متواتر المعنى . وهذا معنى اعتبار الشارع غلبة الظن في الأحكام وصار ذلك بمنزلة نص قطعى من الشارع علما أن كل حكم يغلب على ظن المجتهد فهو ثابت في علم الله ، فيكون ثبوت الحكم المظنون قطعيا فيصح إطلاق العلم على إدراكه . هذا على تقدير تصويب كل مجتهد

yہاں سے فقہ کو قطعی بنانے کی تیسری توجیہ ہے جس کو امام رازی نے اپنی کتاب الحصول میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حکم تو قطعی ہوتا ہے البتہ مجتہد جس طریق اور راستہ سے یعنی غلبہ بطن سے پہنچا ہے، وہ طریق فظنی ہے، جس طرح آپ کو کسی منزل مقصد تک جاتا ہے اپنے انداز سے ایک راستہ پر چل رہے ہیں اور اس راستہ سے حقیقتا آپ منزل مقصود تک پہنچ گئے تو اب مقصود تو آپ کو قطعی طور پر حاصل ہو گیا لیکن وہ راستہ نظنی تھا۔ اس کی مزید توضیح کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ اجماع بھی اس بات پر ہے کہ غلبه وطن واجب العلم ہے اور اخبار آحاد تو بکثرت اس بارے میں آچکی ہیں اگر چہ تو تر اتر لفظی موجود نہیں مگر کثرت کی بناء پر تو اتر معنوی کی حد کو پہنچی ہوئی ہیں تو گویا کہ شارع کی طرف سے بمنزلہ نص قطعی کے ہو گیا ، جو مجتہد کا مظنون ہے وہ عند اللہ ثابت اور قطعی ہے ، لہذا اس وقت فقہ پر علم اور ادراک کا اطلاق درست ہوا۔ یہ تقریر اور توضیح اس وقت ہے جب یہ قول لیا جائے کہ کل مجتهد مصيب.
قال الشارح : " فإن قيل : المظنون ما يحتمل النقيض ، والمعلوم ما لا يحتمله فيتنافيان . قلنا: يكون مظنونا ، فيصير معلوما بملاحظة هذ االقياس ، وهو أنه قد علم كونه مظنونا للمجتهد ، وكل ما علم كونه مظنونا للمجتهد علم كونه ثابتا في نفس الأمر قطعا ، على تصويب كل مجتهد . وأما على تقدير أن المصيب واحد فكأنه ثبت نص قطعی على أن كل حكم غلب على ظن المجتهد ، فهو واجب العمل أو هو ثابت بالنظر إلى الدليل ، وإن لم يكن ثابتا في علم الله تعالى ، فيكون وجوب العمل به أو ثبوته بالنظر إلى الدليل قطعيا ، لكن يلزم على الأول أن يكون الفقه عبارة عن العلم بوجوب العمل بالأحكام، وعلى الثانى أن يكون الثابت بالنظر ألى الدليل الظني وإن لم يعلم ثبوته في الواقع قطعيا ، وأنت تعلم أن الثابت القطعى ما لا يحتمل عدم الثبوت في الواقع . غاية ما أمكن في هذا المقام ذكر بعض المحققين في شرح المنهاج : وهو أن الحكم المظنون للمجتهد يحب العمل به قطعا للدليل القاطع وكل حكم يجب العمل به قطعا علم قطعا أنه حكم الله تعالى ، وإلا لم يجب العلم به وكل ما علم قطعا أنه حكم الله قهو معلوم قطعا ، فكل ما يجب العمل به قطعا معلوم قطعا ، فالحكم المظنون للمجتهد معلوم قطعا ، فالفقه علم قطعى والظن وسيلة إليه . وحاصله إنا لا نسلم أن كل حكم يحب العمل به
When the total number is known... despite that due to the multiplicity of narrators and preoccupation with work and travel, the total number cannot be known, so how can the majority and the imams be known? Moreover, even if we accept, it would necessitate that rulings conveyed through khabar wahid are excluded from fiqh. In any case, the definition given by the author is not free from confusion and discrepancy.
The commentator said: 'His statement: "Then his answer, firstly, indicates that what qiyas manifests with the revelation of the wahi is outside fiqh because it is zanni, and then what is presented by the text (nass) and ijma is only qat'i if their proofs are also qat'i, because rulings established by ahadith are zanni."'
Explanation: The author had answered to make fiqh qat'i that in our view fiqh is the name of those rulings with which revelation has descended or on which ijma has been concluded, and it is obvious that then fiqh becomes qat'i. Here the commentator is pointing out two weaknesses of this answer. First: then rulings for which qiyas is manifest (mazhar) would be excluded from fiqh because they are zanni. Second: those issues of fiqh that are established by khabar wahid would also be excluded because they are zanni; moreover, rulings established by nass or ijma are qat'i only when their proof is qat'i.
The commentator said: 'And thirdly: it is what is mentioned in al-Mahsul and elsewhere, that the ruling is qat'i and the zann is in its path. Its exposition: since ijma has indicated the obligation of acting upon zann, and the ahadith on this matter are numerous, to the point of tawatur ma'nawi. This is the meaning of the Lawgiver's consideration of ghalabat al-zann in rulings, and it became like a qat'i nass from the Lawgiver, knowing that every ruling that becomes the preponderant conjecture of the mujtahid is established in the knowledge of Allah, thus the establishment of the conjectural ruling is qat'i, so the application of 'ilm (knowledge) to its comprehension is correct. This is on the assumption of taswib (that every mujtahid is correct).'
Explanation: This is the third justification to make fiqh qat'i, which Imam Razi mentioned in his book al-Mahsul. He states that the ruling is qat'i, but the path by which the mujtahid reaches it, i.e., ghalabat al-zann, is zanni. He further explains that ijma is also on this that ghalabat al-zann is wajib al-'ilm, and ahadith have come abundantly on this, even if there is no literal tawatur, due to abundance they have reached the level of tawatur ma'nawi. So it is as if from the Lawgiver it has become like a qat'i nass, that what the mujtahid considers zanni is established and qat'i with Allah. So at this point, the application of 'ilm and perception to fiqh is correct. This exposition is when the statement 'kull mujtahid musib' is adopted.
The commentator said: 'If it is said: the maznun is what admits its opposite, and the ma'lum is what does not admit it, so they contradict. We say: it is maznun, then becomes ma'lum by considering this qiyas: that it is known to be maznun for the mujtahid, and everything known to be maznun for the mujtahid is known to be established in reality qat'an, on the assumption of taswib of every mujtahid. And on the assumption that only one is correct, it is as if a qat'i nass has been established that every ruling that becomes the preponderant conjecture of the mujtahid is either wajib al-'amal or is established in consideration of the dalil, even if not established in the knowledge of Allah, then the obligation to act or its establishment in consideration of the dalil is qat'i. But on the first, fiqh would be defined as knowledge of the obligation to act on rulings, and on the second, the establishment in consideration of the zanni dalil, even if its establishment in reality is not known qat'an. And you know that qat'i establishment is what does not admit the possibility of non-establishment in reality. The utmost possible in this regard is what some muhaqqiqin mentioned in Sharh al-Minhaj: that the maznun ruling for the mujtahid is wajib al-'amal qat'an due to a qat'i dalil, and every ruling wajib al-'amal qat'an is known qat'an to be the ruling of Allah, otherwise it would not be wajib al-'ilm, and everything known qat'an to be the ruling of Allah is known qat'an, so every ruling wajib al-'amal qat'an is known qat'an, so the maznun ruling for the mujtahid is known qat'an, so fiqh is qat'i knowledge and zann is a means to it. Its summary: we do not concede that every ruling that is wajib al-'amal...
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is the commentary (sharh) on the third response to the objection that fiqh cannot be called 'ilm because it is based on zann. The commentator explains Imam al-Razi's argument from al-Mahsul. The core claim is that the ruling itself (al-hukm) is certain (qat'i), but the means of arriving at it—the preponderant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) of the mujtahid—is zanni. To prove that the ruling is certain, al-Razi argues that ijma (consensus) and the abundant ahadith on acting upon zann have reached tawatur ma'nawi (a mass of reports with multiple chains, though not identical wording), which constitutes a qat'i proof that whatever a mujtahid concludes with preponderant conjecture is established in Allah's knowledge and thus real and certain. This accords with the position that every mujtahid is correct (taswib). The commentator then addresses an objection: that maznun (conjectural) and ma'lum (known) are opposites. He replies that by considering the definitive proof (the qat'i evidence for acting on zann), the maznun becomes ma'lum—it is known that it is established in reality. For those who hold that only one mujtahid is correct (takhṭī'), the argument still works: the obligation to act on the ruling is certain, even if the ruling itself is not absolutely true in reality. The final refinement from Sharh al-Minhaj clarifies that the maznun ruling is known to be wajib al-'amal qat'an, and that implies it is known to be Allah's ruling, hence it is known qat'an. Thus fiqh is qat'i knowledge, and zann is merely the epistemological means.

Key Terms
قطعي (qat'i): Certain knowledge that does not admit the possibility of its opposite; here referring to the ruling itself and the obligation to act.
ظني (zanni): Probable knowledge that admits its opposite; the means (path) to the ruling is zanni, not the ruling itself.
متواتر المعنى (mutawatir al-ma'na): A concept transmitted through numerous chains of narration with different wordings, reaching a level of certainty in meaning.
تصويب (taswib): The position that every mujtahid is correct in his ijtihad; the text gives arguments on both assumptions (taswib and takhti'a).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third response in this passage, why is fiqh considered certain (qat'i) despite rulings being based on zann?
A) Because all rulings are revealed directly.
B) Because the obligation to act upon zann is established by definitive evidence (ijma and mutawatir meaning).
C) Because mujtahids never make mistakes.
D) Because fiqh is based on qiyas alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that fiqh is certain knowledge because the obligation to act on preponderant conjecture is established by definitive evidence (ijma and tawatur ma'nawi), making every validly derived ruling certain either in reality or in obligation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Applying a Universal Rule via Syllogism
Explains how a general principle yields fiqh rulings through syllogism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply a universal rule (qā'idah kulliyah) as the major premise in a syllogism to derive a fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
A universal rule plus a factual minor premise yields a fiqh ruling via syllogism.

This passage demonstrates a core method in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: using a universal rule (qā'idah kulliyah) as the major premise of a syllogism to derive specific rulings. The rule 'everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib' is combined with the minor premise 'hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' to conclude that hajj is wajib. Understanding this logical structure is essential for systematic juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the universal rule (major premise)
In the text, the universal rule is 'كل مأمور الشارع فهو واجب' (everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib). This rule is a general principle derived from multiple textual evidences in usul al-fiqh.
Such rules are not directly from a single text but are inductively established.
2
Construct the minor premise from the specific case
For the case of hajj, the minor premise is 'الحج مأمور الشارع' (hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver). This is established by referencing the Quranic command for hajj.
The minor premise must be factually correct and verifiable from the sources.
3
Combine to derive the fiqh ruling
Applying the first figure of syllogism: if the major premise is true and the minor premise is true, the conclusion follows necessarily. Here, the conclusion is 'الحج واجب' (hajj is wajib).
This is a deductive proof; the conclusion is binding if both premises are sound.
4
Understand the role of conditions and restrictions
The commentator notes that obtaining the universal rule requires studying the states of proofs and rulings, including conditions and restrictions that affect its application. These are part of usul al-fiqh.
Universal rules are not absolute; they may have exceptions or require detailed investigation.

Wajib? [تواب?] hajj is the minor premise, and wajib is the major premise, and mā'mūr al-shāri' is the middle term. Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver is the minor premise, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib is the major premise, and this is the first figure of syllogism. After these preliminaries, we come to the purpose: the major of this proof is a universal rule, i.e., everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib. Attach to it the minor, which is easily obtainable. The reason it is said to be easily obtainable is because it is easy to obtain: for any ruling you wish to know, make it the subject and make the subject of the universal rule its predicate, then the minor is obtained. For example, here we wanted to know the ruling of hajj; we made it the subject and made the subject of the universal rule "everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib" the predicate, so the minor was obtained: i.e., hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver. Then we attach the major: everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib. Therefore the fiqh result is obtained: hajj is wajib. So this is the meaning of reaching fiqh. The commentator says: keep one thing in mind: to obtain the universal rule, it is necessary to discuss the states of the proofs and the states of the rulings, and similarly it is also necessary to discuss those conditions and restrictions that have an effect in obtaining the universal rule. In any case, all discussions are included in the discussions of usul al-fiqh; knowing them is to know the universal rules, just as the author has explained it so clearly that no further addition is possible.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe explaining how a universal rule (قاعدہ کلیہ) is applied via syllogism to derive fiqh rulings. The author illustrates using the rule 'كل مأمور الشارع فهو واجب' (everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib) as the major premise, with 'الحج مأمور الشارع' (hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver) as the minor premise, concluding that hajj is wajib. The commentator emphasizes that obtaining such universal rules requires studying the states of proofs and rulings, including conditions and restrictions, all of which fall within the science of usul al-fiqh. This demonstrates the importance of usul in deriving specific fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
قاعدہ کلیہ (qā‘idah kulliyah): A universal rule (like 'كل مأمور الشارع فهو واجب') that serves as a major premise in syllogistic reasoning to derive fiqh rulings.
مأمور الشارع (ma’mūr al-shāri‘): Something that is commanded by the Lawgiver (Allah or the Prophet), implying a requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver
B) Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib
C) Hajj is wajib
D) Hajj is a pillar of Islam

Key Takeaway
A universal rule (qā'idah kulliyah) functioning as the major premise, combined with a specific minor premise, yields a fiqh ruling through syllogistic deduction.

Fiqh vs Masail al-Fiqh: The Role of Evidence
Sharh explains why muqallid reaches masail, not fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish fiqh from masail al-fiqh based on the role of evidence and explain why the definition of usul al-fiqh excludes the muqallid.

Core Idea
Fiqh is evidence-based knowledge; a muqallid knows rulings, not fiqh.

This lesson clarifies a crucial nuance in the definition of usul al-fiqh. The science is defined as the rules by which one reaches fiqh—knowledge of rulings from the four evidences. But what about a muqallid, who follows a mujtahid? The commentator explains that the muqallid reaches only the masail (particular rulings), not fiqh itself. Understanding this distinction sharpens your grasp of what it means to be a faqih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base claim
Start with the definition of usul al-fiqh: 'the rules by which one reaches fiqh.' Note that 'fiqh' here means knowledge of shar'i rulings directly from the four evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
2
Recognize the muqallid's limitation
A muqallid follows a mujtahid without independently deriving rulings. He knows the ruling (mas'ala) but not the evidential basis. Thus, his knowledge is not fiqh in the technical sense.
The commentator emphasizes that the muqallid lacks the 'strength' (quwwa) to derive from evidence.
3
Apply the distinction to the definition
If the definition of usul al-fiqh is to include the muqallid, the wording must change from 'to fiqh' to 'to masail al-fiqh.' This preserves the technical precision.
This shows the Hanafi commitment to terminological exactness.
4
Reflect on the epistemological weight
Fiqh implies a direct evidential link (dalil). Without that link, one has masail but not fiqh. This distinction affects who qualifies as a faqih.
Hanafi usul: only a mujtahid achieves fiqh; a muqallid is a follower, not a jurist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : قوله : ولا يقال إلى الفقه “ لأن المقلد يتوصل بقواعده إلى مسائل الفقه لا إلى الفقه الذي هو العلم بالأحكام عن أدلتها الأربع ، لأن علمه بها ليس عن أدلة الأربعة .
تشریح
یعنی اگر تو اصل کو عام مانا جائے اور وہ مقلد کو شامل ہو تو تعریف میں تھوڑی تبدیلی کرنی پڑے گی التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه کے بجائے إلى مسائل الفتہ کہنا پڑے گا شارح اس کی وجہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ فقہ کا مطلب ہے براہ راست ادلہ سے احکام کو معلوم کرنا اور مقلد میں اتنی قوت نہیں ہوتی کہ وہ احکام بر او ر است ادلہ سے تھے ، البتہ یہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ اپنے مجتہد کے اقوال کی وجہ سے مسائل فقہ تک پہنچ سکے۔
The commentator said: His statement: 'and it is not said to fiqh' because the muqallid reaches by his rules the masail of fiqh, not to fiqh which is knowledge of rulings from the four evidences, because his knowledge of them is not from the four evidences. Explanation: That is, if the original (definition) is taken as general and includes the muqallid, then a small change must be made in the definition: instead of 'by which one reaches fiqh', it must be said 'by which one reaches the masail of fiqh'. The commentator explains the reason: fiqh means knowing rulings directly from evidence, and the muqallid does not have that strength to derive rulings from evidence, but he can reach the masail of fiqh through the statements of his mujtahid.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage clarifies a nuance in the definition of usul al-fiqh. The term 'fiqh' in the definition technically means knowledge of rulings derived directly from the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). A muqallid does not have such direct knowledge; he knows rulings only through his mujtahid. Therefore, if one insists on including the muqallid in the definition, the wording must be changed to 'masail al-fiqh' (the particular rulings) rather than 'fiqh' itself. The author follows the order: first quoting the matn, then explaining the reasoning. This highlights the precision required in defining usul al-fiqh as a science for mujtahids only.

Key Terms
فقه (fiqh): Knowledge of shar'i rulings derived from their specific evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
مسائل الفقه (masail al-fiqh): The particular rulings of fiqh, without the requirement of knowing the evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Fiqh is derived from evidence; masail are rulings without evidence.
C) Fiqh includes all rulings; masail are only a subset.
D) Both are the same in terms of evidence.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is evidence-based knowledge; a muqallid possesses masail al-fiqh, not fiqh, because his knowledge lacks the direct evidential derivation from the four sources.

Third Type of Essential Accidents in Usul al-Fiqh
Classification of essential accidents in usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify essential accidents in usul al-fiqh, and explain why the third type is excluded from investigation.

Core Idea
Usul studies only attributes that affect proving or being proven; others are irrelevant.

In usul al-fiqh, we study proofs and rulings by examining their essential accidents—attributes inherent to them. But not all attributes matter. This lesson introduces the third category of essential accidents: those that have no bearing on the function of proof or ruling. Understanding this boundary is crucial for focusing on what is truly relevant in usul and avoiding digressions into theology or linguistics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of essential accidents
The commentator divides essential accidents into three: (1) those actually investigated in usul, (2) those that have an impact on the investigated matters, and (3) those neither investigated nor impactful. Focus on the third category as defined by the exclusion criterion: no entry into the attachment of what is investigated.
The first two categories involve attributes that affect ithbat (proving) and thubut (being proven).
2
List examples of the third category from the text
The passage provides examples: possibility (imkan), power (qudra), origination (hadath), simplicity (basata), composition (tarkib), and linguistic properties of proofs like nominal/verbal sentence, triliteral/quadriliteral roots, and declinable/indeclinable forms.
These are studied in other sciences like kalam (theology) or Arabic grammar, not usul.
3
Apply the exclusion criterion to test new examples
Determine whether a given attribute of a proof or ruling affects its function in proving or being proven. If it does, it falls into category 1 or 2; if not, it belongs to category 3.
For example, 'the proof being from the Quran' affects its authority, so it would be category 1 or 2.
4
Use the carpenter analogy to reinforce understanding
The commentator compares the usul scholar to a carpenter: the carpenter examines wood for qualities relevant to carpentry (e.g., hardness, straightness) but ignores philosophical attributes (e.g., possibility, composition). Similarly, usul only examines attributes relevant to deriving rulings.
The analogy emphasizes the practical, focused nature of usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : " أما الثالث يعنى العوارض الذاتية التي لا يكون مبحوثا عنها في هذا العلم، ولها مدخل فى لحوق ما هى مبحوث عنها من القسمين يعني قسمى العوارض التى للأدلة ، والعوارض التى للأحكام ، وذلك كالإمكان والقدر والحدوث ، والبساطة والتركيب ، وكون الدليل جملة إسمية أو فعلية ثلاثية مفرداته أو رباعية معربة ، أو مبنية إلى غير ذلك مما لا دخل له في الإثبات والثبوت فلا يبحث عنها في الأصول ، وهذا كما أن النجار ينظر فى الخشب من جهة صلابته ، ورقته، وغلظته ، واعوجاجه ، وإستقامته ، ونحو ذلك مما يتعلق بصناعته ، لا من جهة إمكانه وحدوثه وتركبه وبساطته ونحو ذلك .
تشريح
عوراض ذاحیہ تین قسم پر نہیں (۱) مجوعہ (۲) جن کو مجوفہ میں دخل ہے (۳) جو نہ مجموثہ ہیں اور نہ مجوعہ میں ان کا دخل ہے ، جیسے قدیم ہونا ممکن ہونا بسیط مرکب ہونا یا دلیل کا جملہ اسمیہ ہونا فعلیہ ہونا معرب ہونا۔ تو اب شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ عوارض کی تیسری قسم اولہ اور احکام دونوں کے اندر متروک ہے ان تمام عوارضات سے اصول فقہ میں بحث نہیں کی جاتی اس کی توضیح یوں سمجھیں کہ آپ لکڑی نجار (ترکھان) کے پاس لے جائیں تو وہ اپنے فن کی مناسبت سے اس میں دیکھے گا کہ یہ لکڑی خشک ہے یا تر ہے، بخت ہے یا نرم ، موٹی ہے یا پتلی ، ٹیڑھی ہے یا سیدھی لیکن یوں نہیں دیکھے گا کہ آیا قدیم ہے یا حادث کیونکہ ان عوارضات کا اس کے فن سے کوئی تعلق نہیں۔
The commentator said: "As for the third, meaning the essential accidents that are not investigated in this science, but have an entry into the attachment of what is investigated from the two divisions, i.e., the two divisions of accidents that are for proofs and the accidents that are for rulings. That is like possibility, power, origination, simplicity, composition, and whether the proof is a nominal or verbal sentence, its individual words are triliteral or quadriliteral, declinable or indeclinable, and other things that have no bearing on proving and being proven, so they are not investigated in usul. This is like the way the carpenter looks at wood from the perspective of its hardness, softness, thickness, crookedness, straightness, and similar things related to his craft, not from the perspective of its possibility, origination, composition, simplicity, and the like."
Commentary: The essential accidents are of three types: (1) those that are discussed [in usul], (2) those that have an entry into what is discussed, and (3) those that are neither discussed nor have entry. Examples: being eternal, possible, simple, compound, or the proof being a nominal or verbal sentence, declinable, etc. Now the commentator says that the third type of accidents is abandoned in both proofs and rulings; all these accidents are not discussed in usul al-fiqh. Understand this with an analogy: if you take wood to a carpenter, he will look at it according to his craft: whether it is dry or wet, hard or soft, thick or thin, crooked or straight. But he will not look at whether it is eternal or originated, because these accidents have no relation to his craft.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of essential accidents ('awaridh dhatiya) in usul al-fiqh. The essential accidents of proofs and rulings are divided into three types: (1) those that are actually investigated in usul (e.g., being general or specific), (2) those that have an impact on the matters investigated, and (3) those that are neither investigated nor have any impact. The third type includes attributes like possibility (imkan), eternality (qidam), origination (hadath), simplicity (basatah), composition (tarkib), and linguistic properties of the proof (e.g., nominal vs. verbal sentence, triliteral vs. quadriliteral roots, declinable vs. indeclinable). These do not affect the function of proofs in establishing rulings or the nature of rulings themselves, so usul does not study them. The commentator uses the analogy of a carpenter: he examines wood for qualities relevant to carpentry (hardness, softness, thickness, straightness) but not for philosophical attributes like possibility or composition. This clarifies the specific focus of usul al-fiqh on matters directly related to deriving rulings from proofs.

Key Terms
العوارض الذاتية (al-'awaridh al-dhatiyya): Essential accidents or attributes that can belong to a thing in the context of a specific science, classified here into three types based on relevance.
الإمكان (al-imkan): Possibility of existence; an attribute irrelevant to usul al-fiqh.
القسم الثالث (al-qism al-thalith): The third category of essential accidents, neither investigated nor having an impact on what is investigated in usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Whether a proof is a nominal or verbal sentence.
C) Whether a ruling is obligatory (wajib) or prohibited (haram).
D) Whether a proof is from the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh excludes essential accidents that do not affect the function of proving or being proven, focusing only on those attributes directly relevant to deriving rulings from proofs.

6 min
The Function of Dalil is Independent of Hukm's Temporality
Critical commentary on the irrelevance of hukm's nature to the function of dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the eternal or temporal nature of a ruling (hukm) does not affect the function of a legal proof (dalīl) in providing knowledge, and identify the inclusive definition of ʿilm in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A legal proof gives knowledge of existence or non-existence, regardless of whether the ruling is eternal or temporal.

In this passage, the commentator refutes a claim that the nature of the hukm (ruling)—whether eternal like Allah's attribute or temporal like a revealed command—could alter the function of the dalīl (proof). He insists that the sole purpose of a dalīl is to provide knowledge (ʿilm) of the existence or non-existence of something. This knowledge is defined broadly to include both certain and probable knowledge, so it applies to all types of proofs. Understanding this clarifies a foundational principle in usul al-fiqh: the proof's indicatory function is independent of the proven's ontological status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of the critique
Locate the claim that the commentator rejects. The passage begins by referring to 'His statement: If by hukm is meant...' and then dismisses it as 'speech with no benefit'. Identify the implied position that the definition of hukm could affect the dalil.
The target is an argument that attempts to link the nature of the hukm (eternal/temporal) to the validity or function of the proof.
2
State the commentator's core argument
The commentator asserts that legal proofs are 'identifiers and indicators'. Even if one concedes they are 'proofs in reality', their meaning is nothing except providing knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing. This is the essential function.
The phrase 'ما يفيد العلم بثبوت الشئ أو انتفائه' (what gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing) is the key definition.
3
Analyze the definition of ʿilm
The commentator explains that 'knowledge' (ʿilm) here is taken in a broad sense: 'firm or preponderant perception' (الإدراك الحازم أو الراجح) to include both certain (qaṭʿī) and probable (ẓannī) knowledge. This makes the definition applicable to all types of proofs (e.g., mutawatir and ahad).
This broad definition is typical of Hanafi usul, allowing a wide range of sources to function as valid proofs.
4
Explain why temporality does not matter
The commentator concludes that the function of the proof does not differ whether the ruling is eternal (qadīm) or temporal (ḥādith). The proof indicates the existence of the ruling regardless of when or how the ruling exists. The ontological status of the madlul does not affect the indicatory function of the dalil.
This shields the theory of proof from metaphysical disputes about the nature of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : " قوله : " إن أريد بـالـحـكـم " هذا كلام لا حاصل له ، لأن الأدلة الشرعية معرفات وإمارات ، ولو سلم أنها أدلة حقيقة ، فلا معنى للدليل إلا ما يفيد العلم بثبوت الشئ أو انتفائه . غاية ما في الباب أن العلم يؤخذ بمعنى الإدراك الحازم او الراجح ليعم القطعى والظني ، فيصح في جميع الأدلة ، وهذا لا يتفاوت بقدم الحكم وحدوثه ،
The commentator said: 'His statement: "If by hukm is meant..." this is a speech with no benefit, because the legal proofs are identifiers and indicators. Even if it is conceded that they are proofs in reality, the meaning of proof is nothing except what gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing. The most that can be said is that knowledge is taken in the sense of firm or preponderant perception to include both certain and probable, so it applies to all proofs. And this does not differ whether the ruling is eternal or temporal.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of an argument about the definition of hukm (ruling). The commentator rejects a claim that if hukm is defined in a certain way (perhaps as eternal or temporal), it would affect the nature of proof. He argues that legal proofs are indicators that lead to knowledge of existence or non-existence. The definition of knowledge used here is broad enough to include both certain and probable knowledge, thus covering all types of proofs. Whether the hukm itself is eternal (qadīm, as in the case of Allah's attribute) or temporal (ḥādith, as in revelatory commands) does not change the fact that the proof indicates it. Thus, the definition of hukm is irrelevant to the function of dalil. This clarifies the relationship between dalil and madlūl (the proven).

Key Terms
دليل (dalīl): What provides knowledge of the existence or non-existence of something
علم (ʿilm): Firm or preponderant perception, includes certain (qaṭʿī) and probable (ẓannī)
حكم (ḥukm): The thing proven by the dalil, either eternal or temporal

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only certain knowledge (qaṭʿī)
B) Only probable knowledge (ẓannī)
C) Both certain and probable knowledge
D) Only knowledge from rational proofs

Key Takeaway
The function of a legal proof (dalīl) is to provide knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a ruling, and this function is unaffected by whether the ruling is eternal or temporal.

8 min
The Definition of Dalil: An Indicator, Not a Cause
Critique of the matn's lengthy discussion on dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of dalil as an amara that gives knowledge of the hukm, and explain why it does not establish the hukm itself.

Core Idea
Dalil is an indicator (amara) that gives knowledge of the hukm, not a cause that brings the hukm into existence.

In this passage, the commentator critiques the matn's prolonged discussion about whether the hukm is qadim or hadith and how dalil relates to it. The commentator argues that such detail is unnecessary because shar'i evidences are merely indicators (amarat) that lead to knowledge (ilm) or predominant probability (ghalabat al-zann) of the hukm, not causes that establish the hukm itself. This distinction is crucial: it means that dalil is epistemological, not ontological.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
This passage centers on the definitions of dalil (دلیل) and hukm (حکم). Note their meanings in the text: dalil is something that gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing; hukm can be the eternal address of Allah or the juristic classification of wujub/hurma.
2
Understand the matn's position
The matn had suggested that if hukm is qadim (eternal), then dalil only gives knowledge of the hukm; if hukm is hadith (created), then dalil might establish the hukm itself. This led to a lengthy discussion.
3
Follow the commentator's refutation
The commentator argues that such detail is unnecessary because shar'i evidences are not real causes (ilal) but identifiers (amarat). Regardless of whether hukm is qadim or hadith, dalil only gives knowledge, not thubut (establishment).
The commentator defines dalil as 'that which gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing'—this applies universally.
4
Examine the final concession
The matn himself is forced to agree: 'We intend in all that the establishment of knowledge for us or the predominance of probability (ghalabat al-zann).' Thus the prolonged discussion was unnecessary.
This shows that the matn's earlier distinction between qadim/hadith does not affect the core function of dalil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أضطر إلى ذلك إلى آخر الأمر . وليس معنى الدليل ما يفيد نفس الثبوت كما هو شان العلل الخارجية وإن جعلنا الحكم حادثا على ما يشعر به كلامه. تشریح: ماتن نے کہا تھا کہ اگر حکم سے خطاب اللہ مراد ہو جو قدیم ہے تو پھر ادلہ سے ثابت ہونے کا مطلب ہوگا علم ثبوت الحکم کیونکہ خود حکم دلیل سے ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا اس لیے کہ قدیم ہے اور اگر حکم سے مراد اصطلاح فقہاء ہو وجوب اور حرمت تو پھر خود حکم کا ثبوت مراد ہو گا۔ اب یہاں سے شارح ماتن کی تردید کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ سں قدر تطویل کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ، اس لیے کہ ادلہ شرعیہ معرفات اور امارات ہیں جن سے حکم کا علم حاصل ہوتا ہے، خود حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا اور اگر ان کو ادلہ حقیقہ تسلیم بھی کر لیا جائے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ دلیل وہ ہوتی ہے جس سے علم بثبوت الشئ یا انتفاء الشئ حاصل ہو تو اس سے حکم کے قدیم یا حادث ہونے سے فرق نہیں پڑتا ۔ اور اگر حکم کو حادث مانیں تو پھر بھی دلیل سے اس کا علم حاصل ہوگا نہ کہ دلیل حکم کو ثابت کرے گی، زیادہ سے زیادہ علم کو عام معنی میں لینا پڑے گا کہ علم بثبوت الحکم سے مراد عام ہے الادراك الحازم یعنی یقین یا الراجح یعنی نلمن غالب اور ماتن بھی بالآ خر اسی بات کی طرف مجبور ہوا ہے اور کہا ہے کہ فنقول : نريد في جميع ذلك إثبات العلم لنا أو غلبة الظن تو خواہ مخواہ اتنی طوالت کرنے کی ضرورت کیا ہے۔
And he was compelled to that in the end. And the meaning of dalil is not what conveys the very establishment (thubut) as is the case of external causes, even if we consider the hukm as hadith as his words suggest. Commentary: The matn had said that if by hukm is meant the address of Allah which is qadim, then the meaning of being established by evidences is the knowledge of the establishment of the hukm, because the hukm itself cannot be established by a dalil since it is qadim; and if by hukm is meant the juristic terminology of wujub and hurma, then the establishment of the hukm itself is intended. Here the commentator wants to refute the matn, saying that such prolongation is unnecessary, because the shar'i evidences are identifiers and indicators that give knowledge of the hukm; they do not establish the hukm itself. And even if we accept them as real evidences, we say that dalil is that which gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing; then it does not matter whether the hukm is qadim or hadith. And if we consider the hukm as hadith, still the dalil will give knowledge of it, not that the dalil establishes the hukm. At most, we must take knowledge in a general sense: knowledge of the establishment of the hukm in the general meaning of perception (idrak hazim) i.e. certainty, or the predominant (al-rajih) i.e. the predominant probability (ghalabat al-zann). And the matn too was forced to this in the end, saying: 'We intend in all that the establishment of knowledge for us or the predominance of probability (ghalabat al-zann).' So why was such prolongation necessary?
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn's discussion regarding the definition of dalil and its function. The matn had debated whether the hukm is qadim (eternal) or hadith (created), and whether dalil proves the hukm itself or merely gives knowledge of it. The commentator argues that the matn's prolonged discussion is unnecessary because shar'i evidences are not real causes (ilal) that bring the hukm into existence; they are merely indicators (amarat) that lead to knowledge of the hukm. The commentator defines dalil as that which gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of something, regardless of whether the hukm is qadim or hadith. Even if the hukm is hadith, the dalil still only gives knowledge, not actual existence. The commentator concludes by noting that the matn himself was forced to accept this position, as seen in his statement that we intend 'establishment of knowledge for us or predominance of probability.' Thus, the lengthy discussion was unnecessary.

Key Terms
دلیل (dalil): An indicator that gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of a thing.
حکم (hukm): Either the eternal address of Allah or the juristic classification (wujub/hurma).
أمارة (amara): An indicator that leads to predominant probability (ghalabat al-zann) or certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the main problem with the matn's discussion?
A) The matn is wrong about the hukm being qadim.
B) The matn unnecessarily prolongs the discussion.
C) The matn confuses dalil with 'illa.
D) The matn denies that dalil gives knowledge.

Key Takeaway
A dalil in Hanafi usul is an indicator (amara) that leads to knowledge or predominant probability of the hukm; it does not establish the hukm itself.
